Application to Ushr and Kharaj: Actual vs Estimated Produce
Application of ability types to ushr and kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between qudra mumkina and qudra muyassara to ushr and kharaj, explaining why kharaj can be due by estimated ability while ushr requires actual produce.

Core Idea
Ushr requires actual produce (qudra muyassara based on real yield); kharaj can be based on estimated ability to cultivate.

The passage extends the division of ability to agricultural taxes: ushr (tithe) and kharaj (land tax). Ushr is tied to the actual produce (al-kharij al-tahqiqi) and is obligatory by qudra muyassara. In contrast, kharaj is based on the land's potential and can be imposed even if the land is neglected, due to estimated ability (qudra taqdiriya). However, fatwa is not given based on this due to oppression. This lesson explores the practical difference and the role of estimated ability.

Guided Path
1
Recall the two types of ability
Qudra mumkina (possible) vs qudra muyassara (facilitated). Understand that qudra muyassara requires ease and continuity.
This lesson focuses on qudra muyassara in agricultural obligations.
2
Analyze ushr: condition of actual produce
Ushr is a share of the actual harvest (ushr is an 'ism idafi', an additional name implying a portion of something existing). It is only due when produce exists. If the produce is lost after ability to give, the ushr drops proportionally.
The passage says 'العشر واجب بالقدرة الميسرة' and requires 'الخارج التحقيقي' (actual produce).
3
Analyze kharaj: estimated ability
Kharaj is also by qudra muyassara, but it is conditioned on ability to cultivate (water, tools). If the land is neglected, kharaj is still due based on estimated ability (التمكن التقديري) because the owner could have cultivated.
But fatwa is not given on this due to fear of oppressors taking advantage.
4
Contrast the two: actual vs estimated
Ushr requires actual produce; kharaj can be based on estimated ability. This is because kharaj is a tax on the land itself (a duty that remains even if not cultivated), while ushr is a share of the crop.
If a natural disaster destroys the crop after cultivation, kharaj drops (because the facilitated ability is lost).
5
Relate back to the division of ability
Both ushr and kharaj are by qudra muyassara, but the precise condition differs: actual existence for ushr, potential for cultivation for kharaj. This shows that qudra muyassara can be calibrated.
The passage ends by contrasting with hajj and sadaqat al-fitr as qudra mumkina.

إذ لو بقيت عليه لم يكن إلا غُرما، وعند الشافعي : لا تسقط لتقرر الوجوب عليه بالتمكن، بخلاف ما إذا استهلكه؛ إذ تبقى عليه زجرا له على التعدي، وهذا إذا هلك النصاب كله؛ إذ لو هلك بعض النصاب تبقى بقسطه؛ لأن شرط النصاب في الابتداء لم يكن إلا للغناء لا لليسر؛ إذ أداء درهم من أربعين كأداء خمسة دراهم من مائتين، فإذا وجد الغناء، ثم هلك البعض، فاليسر في الباقي باق بقدر حصته. أي في القدر الباقي. وكذا العشر كان واجبًا بالقدرة الميسرة؛ لأن الممكنة فيه كان بنفس الزراعة، فإذا شرط قيام تسعة الأعشار عنده كان دليلاً على أنه يجب بطريق اليسر، فإذا هلك الخارج كله أو بعضه بعد التمكن من التصدق تبطل العشر بحصته؛ لأنه اسم إضافي يقتضي وجود الحصص الباقية. ما هلك الصغر إذ لو بقيت أي الزكاة، وهذا يرشدك إلى أن المراد بالسقوط السقوط في الدارين كما اختاره في "مشكاة الأنوار"، وقال صاحب "التقرير": إن السقوط بالهلاك إنما هو في أحكام الدنيا وأما في المؤاخذة فيأثم بعد التمكن. (القمر) إذ لو بقيت إلخ يعني لو بقيت مقدار الواجب المقدم، فإما أن يجب من حيث الزكاة وذا متعذر؛ لأنها كانت واجبة بالقدرة الميسرة، وقد فاتت فلو وجبت بدونها يلزم قلب الموضوع وعكس المشروع، وإما أن يجب من حيث الضمان والغرم وهذا أيضًا متعذر؛ لأن الضمان يستدعي سبق التعدي، وههنا لم يوجد التعدي و لم يتحقق صنع منه، بل أخذه صاحب الحق بخلاف الاستهلاك لأنه يصنعه . (السنبلي)
لا تسقط أي الزكاة بهلاك النصاب بعد تمام الحول. (القمر) زجرًا له على التعدي: أي على حق الغير، وذا يوجب الغرم عليه، فالنصاب كأنه باق تقديرًا في حق صاحب الحق. (القمر)
:وهذا أي الخلاف بيننا وبين الشافعي . (القمر) تبقى أي الزكاة بقسط الباقي. (القمر) للغناء: أي ليصير المكلف به أهلاً للوجوب، فإن المطلوب من الزكاة إغناء الفقير والإغناء بصفة الحسن لا يتحقق من غير الغني كالتمليك لا يتحقق من غير المالك، وأحوال الناس متفاوتة في الغناء، فقدره الشارع بملك النصاب، فالنصاب كالقدرة الممكنة في العبادات البدنية. (القمر)
لا لليسر : إذ الواجب ربع العشر وأداء درهم من أربعين كأداء خمسة دراهم من مائتين في اليسر. (القمر) فإذا شرط إلخ : لأن العشر تعلق بحقيقة الخارج الذي هو نماء الأرض، وهو ما يحصل بالزراعة.(القمر)

مبحث الخاص
١٤١
بيان تقسيم القدرة
وكذا الخراج كان واجبًا بالقدرة الميسرة؛ لأنه تشترط فيه التمكن من الزراعة بنزول المطر ووجود آلات الحرث وغير ذلك، فإذا عطّل الأرض و لم يزرع يجب عليه الخراج للتمكن التقديري وهذا مما يعرف ولا يفتى به لتجاسر الظلمة، بخلاف العشر؛ فإنه يشترط فيه الخارج التحقيقي دون التقديري، ولكن إذا لم يعطل وزرع الارض، واصطلمت الزرع آفة يسقط عنه الخراج؛ لأنه واجب بالقدرة الميسرة.
بخلاف الأولى حتى لا يسقط الحج وصدقة الفطر بهلاك المال، بيان للممكنة بطريق أي القدرة الممكنة المقابلة يعني أن بقاء القدرة الممكنة ليس بشرط لبقاء الواجب؛ لأنه شرط محض ولا يشترط بقاؤه كالشهود في باب النكاح، فإذا زالت القدرة الممكنة يبقى الواجب، ولهذا يبقى الحج وصدقة الفطر بهلاك المال؛ لأنه إلخ أي لأن الخراج من مؤون الأرض، وتعلق وجوب الخراج بنماء الأرض لا برقبة الأرض حتى لو كانت الأرض سنجة، فلا يجب شيء، فيشترط فيه إلخ وهذا يسر. (القمر)
فإذا عطل إلخ : جواب سؤال وهو: أنه لو كان الخراج واجبًا بصفة اليسر لما وجب على من عطل الأرض و لم يزرع؛ لأنه لا يسر على وجوب الخراج عليه، وحاصل الجواب: أن وجوب الخراج عليه للتمكن التقديري لتقصيره كأنه استهلك، والخراج لما ليس من جنس الخارج فأمكن فيه اعتبار الخارج التقديري للتمكن، فهو بخلاف العشر فإنه اسم إضافي فيشترط فيه الخارج التحقيقي ليبقى تسعة أعشار عند صاحب الأرض. (القمر) لتجاسر الظلمة إلخ لأنهم لا يعذرونه في حال بل يقولون إنك عطلت الأرض و لم تزرع مع تمكنك من الزراعة وإن كان الواقعة بخلاف ذلك، فيلزمون عليه الخراج ظلمًا مع عدم لزومه عليه في الحقيقة. (السنبلي) لأنه واجب إلخ فلو بقي الخراج بعد اصطلام الآفة الزرع لكان غرما ، فانقلب اليسير إلى العسير.(القمر) لأنه شرط محض إلخ توضيحه: أن القدرة الممكنة شرط محض للتمكن من إحداث الفعل، وليس فيها بمعنى العلة، فلم يشترط بقاؤها لبقاء الواجب، فإن البقاء غير الوجود، وما هو شرط الوجود لا يلزم أن يكون شرط البقاء، ألا ترى أن الشهود في النكاح شرط لانعقاد النكاح، ولا يشترط بقاءهم لبقاء النكاح، بخلاف القدرة الميسرة، فإنها ليست شرطًا محضا، بل فيها معنى العلة تفيد صفة في الواجب، وهي صفة اليسر، فأوجبت الواجب بصفة اليسر، فالواجب ليس مشروعًا إلا بصفة اليسر ولا يتصور اليسر بدون القدرة الميسرة، فلذا يشترط بقاء القدرة الميسرة لبقاء الواجب. (القمر)
Section on al-Khass. 140. Explanation of the division of ability. For if it remained upon him, it would only be a burden. And according to al-Shafi'i: it does not drop because the obligation is established upon him by ability. Contrary to if he consumed it; for it remains upon him as a deterrent for transgression. And this is if the entire nisab is lost; for if part of the nisab is lost, it remains proportionally. Because the condition of nisab initially was only for sufficiency, not for ease; for paying one dirham from forty is like paying five dirhams from two hundred in terms of ease. So when sufficiency is found, then part is lost, ease remains in the remaining portion proportionally. Similarly, 'ushr was obligatory by facilitated ability because possible ability in it was by cultivation itself. So when it is conditioned that nine-tenths remain with him, it is evidence that it is obligatory by way of ease. So if the produce is lost entirely or partially after being able to give charity, the 'ushr becomes void proportionally because it is an additional name requiring the existence of remaining portions. ... And also kharaj was obligatory by facilitated ability because it is conditioned in it the ability to cultivate by rainfall, existence of tools, etc. So if he neglects the land and does not cultivate, kharaj is due on him due to estimated ability. This is known but not given as a fatwa due to the audacity of oppressors. Unlike 'ushr, for it requires actual produce, not estimated. But if he does not neglect and cultivates, and a pest destroys the crop, kharaj drops from him because it was obligatory by facilitated ability. Contrary to the first case so that Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr do not drop by loss of wealth. Explanation of possible ability: that the continuation of possible ability is not a condition for the continuation of the obligation because it is a pure condition and its continuation is not required, like witnesses in marriage. So if possible ability is removed, the obligation remains. Hence Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr remain even if wealth is lost. ...
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul discussion explaining the division of ability (qudra) into two types: possible ability (qudra mumkina) and facilitated ability (qudra muyassara). The author uses examples from zakat, ushr, and kharaj to illustrate how each type functions as a condition for obligation. The key principle: possible ability is a pure condition (shart mahd) for the initial obligation; once the obligation is established, it does not need to persist. Thus, if one loses the nisab after the year, zakat still remains due according to al-Shafi'i, but the Hanafi position is that it drops because the obligation was tied to facilitated ability (the ease of paying from surplus). However, if the nisab is partially lost, the obligation remains proportionally. For ushr (tithe), the obligation is by facilitated ability—it arises from the actual produce, so if the produce is lost after ability to pay, the obligation drops. For kharaj (land tax), it is also by facilitated ability—if the land is neglected, kharaj is due by estimated ability; but if the crop is destroyed by a natural disaster, it drops. The passage then contrasts this with possible ability examples like Hajj and Sadaqat al-Fitr: even if one loses the wealth after the obligation is due, the obligation remains because possible ability was only a condition for the initial obligation. The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sanbali explains these points in detail.

Key Terms
التمكن التقديري (al-tamakkun al-taqdiri): Estimated ability to cultivate; used as a basis for kharaj if land is neglected.
الخارج التحقيقي (al-kharij al-tahqiqi): Actual produce; required for ushr.
اسم إضافي (ism idafi): Additional name; ushr is an ism idafi because it implies a portion of something that exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is fatwa not given on the ruling that kharaj is due on neglected land?
A) The ruling is in dispute and not accepted by all scholars.
B) Oppressors might misuse the ruling to impose unjust taxes.
C) The ruling only applies to certain types of land.
D) The ruling was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Ushr requires actual produce; kharaj can be based on estimated ability, but fatwa on that is withheld to prevent oppression.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy

Definition and Ruling of Muawwal (al-Muawwal)
Defining muawwal as a homonym preponderated by dominant opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define muawwal, explain its place in the nazm hierarchy, and distinguish it from mufassar and other categories.

Core Idea
Muawwal: a mushtarak settled by dominant conjecture, yet its ruling is attributed to the expression as if explicit.

In Hanafi usul, texts are classified by clarity. Muawwal occupies an important intermediate category: it is a mushtarak that has been interpreted to one meaning by predominant opinion. Although this interpretation depends on the mujtahid's act, the ruling is considered as if it originated from the text itself. Understanding muawwal is key to grasping how Hanafis handle ambiguous legal language.

Guided Path
1
Define muawwal
From the source, muawwal is a mushtarak whose one meaning is preponderated by ghalib al-ra'y (predominant conjecture).
It is not simply a homonym; it has been resolved to one meaning.
2
Understand the role of tarjih
The preponderance is by predominant conjecture (zann ghalib), not certainty. If it were definitive, it would be mufassar.
This distinguishes muawwal from mufassar.
3
Identify its classification in nazm
Though interpretation is an act of the mujtahid, the ruling is attributed to the expression itself, so muawwal is counted among divisions of nazm (textual structure).
The passage argues that it follows the mushtarak, which is fundamentally part of nazm.
4
Distinguish from other categories
Khafi, mushkil, and mujmal, when clarified by a speculative proof, become muawwal but are considered divisions of bayan (clarification), not nazm.
This passage focuses on muawwal after mushtarak.
5
Address the objections
The passage responds to three anticipated objections: (1) muawwal should not be in nazm, (2) the definition may not include khabar wahid, (3) 'dominant opinion' is not limited to ijtihad.
Each objection is refuted with logical responses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المؤول
تعريف المؤول وحكمه
فقال: وأما المؤول: فما ترجّح من المشترك بعض وجوهه بغالب الرأي يعني أن المشترك مادام لم يترجح أحد معنييه على الآخر فهو مشترك، وإذا ترجّح أحد معنييه بتأويل المجتهد صار ذلك المشترك بعينه مؤولاً . وإنما عدّ من أقسام النظم وإن حصل بفعل التأويل؛ الذي هو فعل المجتهد لأن الحكم بعد التأويل يضاف إلى الصيغة، فكأن النصّ ورد بهذا، وإنما قيد بقوله: من أي بهذا الحكم المشترك؛ لأن المراد ههنا هو هذا المؤول الذي بعد المشترك، وإلا فالخفي والمشكل
والمجمل إذا زال خفاؤها بدليل ظني صار مؤولاً أيضًا، ولكنه من أقسام البيان، والمراد
كخبر الواحد والقياس
بغالب الرأي الظن الغالب، سواء حصل بخبر الواحد أو القياس أو نحوه، فلا يقال:
من حيث قيل حقيقة فقط، وقيل: لا حقيقة ولا مجازا . المحشي) وإنما عد إلخ: دفع إشكال مقدر تقريره: أن المراد من المؤول يظهر بغلب الرأي، فلا يكون حينئذٍ من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة. (القمر) يضاف إلخ لأن إضافة الحكم إلى الدليل الأقوى أولى، فأثر الرأي إنما هو في إظهار المراد من المشترك، ولك أن تقول: إن إضافة الحكم بعد التأويل إلى مجرد الصيغة ممنوع، وأما إلى الصيغة بانضمام التأويل فمسلّم لكنه غير نافع، وقد يجاب عن الإشكال بأن عدّ المؤول من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة إنما هو بتبعية المشترك الذي هو من

(القمر) والمراد بغالب الرأي إلخ لما كان متبادر من غالب الرأي رأي المجتهد أي اجتهاده، فيتوهم منه أن ترجيح المشترك إنما يكون باجتهاد المجتهد لا بغيره فدفع هذا بقوله : والمراد إلخ، وأراد بالرأي الظن سواء كان باجتهاد أي القياس الشرعي أو بالقرائن أو بخبر الواحد.(السنبلي)
الظن الغالب فلو كان صارف اللفظ إلى بعض محتملاته قطعيًا سميناه مفسراً. (القمر)
أو نحوه: كالتأمل في الصيغة كما في ثلاثة قروء. (القمر)
Topic of the Interpreted (Muawwal): Definition of Muawwal and its Ruling. He said: As for the muawwal: it is that whose some aspects of the mushtarak are preponderated by predominant opinion meaning that the mushtarak as long as neither of its two meanings is preponderated over the other, it is mushtarak. When one of its meanings is preponderated by the interpretation (ta'wil) of the mujtahid, that same mushtarak becomes muawwal. It is counted among the divisions of the structure (nazm) even though it occurs by the act of interpretation which is the act of the mujtahid because the ruling after interpretation is attributed to the expression, as if the text had come with this. He restricted by his statement: 'from' meaning by this ruling of the mushtarak, because what is intended here is this muawwal that comes after the mushtarak. Otherwise, the khafi, mushkil, and mujmal when their obscurity is removed by a speculative proof (dalil zanni) become muawwal as well, but it is from the divisions of bayan. And what is intended by dominant opinion is the predominant conjecture, whether it occurs by khabar wahid or qiyas or the like, so it is not said: From where it is said only literal, and it is said: neither literal nor metaphorical. (al-Muhashi?) And why it is counted etc.: a response to an anticipated objection: the meaning of muawwal appears by predominant opinion, so it would then not be from the divisions of the structure in wording and language. (al-Qamar) It is attributed etc.: because attributing the ruling to the stronger evidence is more appropriate. The effect of opinion is only in manifesting the intended meaning from the mushtarak. You can say: attributing the ruling after interpretation to the bare expression is not allowed, but to the expression with the addition of interpretation it is conceded but not beneficial. It can be answered that counting muawwal as from the divisions of the structure in wording and language is only by following the mushtarak, which is from the divisions of the structure in wording and language, not fundamentally. So ponder. (al-Qamar) It is from the divisions of bayan, not from the divisions of the structure in wording and language. (al-Qamar) And the intended by dominant etc.: a response to an anticipated objection: the muawwal may have preponderance by khabar wahid and the definition of the matn does not include it, so it is not comprehensive. The summary of the response: he mentioned the specific and intended the general, or the necessary and intended the implication. (al-Qamar) And the intended by dominant opinion etc.: because what is immediately understood from 'dominant opinion' is the opinion of the mujtahid, i.e., his ijtihad. So it might be misunderstood that preponderance of the mushtarak only occurs by the ijtihad of the mujtahid and not otherwise. So he refuted this by saying: and the intended etc. He intended by 'opinion' the conjecture whether by ijtihad i.e. legal analogy, or by contextual indications, or by khabar wahid. (al-Sunbuliyyah) The predominant conjecture. If the factor turning the word to some of its probabilities is definitive, we call it mufassar. (al-Qamar) Or the like: like pondering upon the expression as in the case of three qur'. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage defines muawwal (the interpreted text) and discusses its ruling. Muawwal is a mushtarak (homonym) whose one of its possible meanings is preponderated (tarjih) by a dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y). The passage clarifies that muawwal is considered part of the divisions of nazm (textual structure) even though the preponderance occurs by the act of interpretation (ta'wil) by a mujtahid. This is because after interpretation, the ruling is attributed to the expression itself, as if the text had been revealed with that meaning. The passage also distinguishes muawwal from other categories like khafi, mushkil, and mujmal which, when clarified by a speculative proof, become muawwal but are considered part of bayan (clarification) not nazm. The dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y) is defined as predominant conjecture (zann ghalib), whether achieved through khabar wahid, qiyas, or other means. The commentary addresses potential objections: first, that if muawwal is based on opinion, it should not be counted as part of nazm; the response is that it follows the mushtarak which is part of nazm. Second, if muawwal can be based on khabar wahid, the definition might be too narrow; the response is that the definition uses the specific term 'dominant opinion' to include general means. Third, clarifying that 'opinion' here means conjecture, not just ijtihad, to avoid the misunderstanding that only ijtihad can preponderate meanings.

Key Terms
المؤول (al-muawwal): A mushtarak whose one meaning is preponderated by dominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y).
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-ra'y): Predominant conjecture (zann ghalib) that leads to preponderance, whether from textual evidence, analogy, or contextual indications.
التأويل (al-ta'wil): The act of interpreting a text by preferring one of its possible meanings based on evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what distinguishes muawwal from mufassar?
A) Mufassar is based on definitive evidence, muawwal on predominant conjecture.
B) Mufassar is a type of mushtarak, muawwal is not.
C) Muawwal requires ijma, mufassar does not.
D) Muawwal is always from the Quran, mufassar from hadith.

Key Takeaway
Muawwal is a mushtarak whose meaning is settled by predominant conjecture, and its ruling is treated as if it were explicitly stated in the text.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
8 min
Definition of Mu'awwal and Its Status in Hanafi Usul
Defining mu'awwal and its relation to nazm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'awwal, identify its conditions, and explain why it is counted as part of the textual divisions (nazm) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A mushtarak becomes mu'awwal when a mujtahid's predominant opinion preponderates one meaning, and it is treated as part of the text itself.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of mu'awwal—an interpreted text that arises from a homonym (mushtarak) when one meaning is given preponderance by the mujtahid's dominant speculation (zann ghalib). This passage from Nur al-Anwar explains the technical definition and addresses a subtle debate about whether mu'awwal belongs to the textual divisions (nazm) or not. Understanding mu'awwal is crucial for grasping the Hanafi hierarchy of textual clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term and its genus
Mu'awwal is defined as a mushtarak (homonym) whose one meaning is preponderated by dominant opinion. Start by recognizing that mu'awwal is not an independent category but a transformed state of mushtarak.
Mushtarak is a word with multiple possible meanings without preponderance at the outset.
2
Determine the cause (sabab) of transformation
The transformation from mushtarak to mu'awwal occurs through ta'wil (interpretation) by a mujtahid. This interpretation must be based on predominant opinion (ghalib al-ra'y), which is a speculative (zanni) preponderance.
Ta'wil is the act of giving preponderance to one meaning.
3
Examine the condition (shart) for mu'awwal
The preponderance must be speculative (zanni), not definitive (qat'i). If the evidence is definitive, the text becomes mufassar, not mu'awwal. Also, the source of preponderance can be khabar wahid, qiyas, or contextual clues.
The example of 'quru' shows contextual reflection as a basis.
4
Understand the legal effect (athar)
Once mu'awwal, the text is treated as if it definitively carried that meaning for the purpose of deriving rulings. The ruling is attributed to the sighah (formula) itself, not merely to the interpreter's effort.
This justifies counting mu'awwal among divisions of nazm.
5
Analyze the debate about inclusion in nazm
The Hanafi position is that mu'awwal is part of nazm because the ruling is added to the sighah. Some unnamed opponents object that ta'wil is a human act, so the text should not be considered part of the original nazm. The response: mu'awwal follows mushtarak, which is already nazm, and the effect of interpretation is only to manifest the intended meaning.
This debate has implications for how mu'awwal texts are cited in proofs.

Source Text

وأما المؤول: فما ترجّح من المشترك بعض وجوهه بغالب الرأي يعني أن المشترك مادام لم يترجح أحد معنييه على الآخر فهو مشترك، وإذا ترجّح أحد معنييه بتأويل المجتهد صار ذلك المشترك بعينه مؤولاً . وإنما عدّ من أقسام النظم وإن حصل بفعل التأويل؛ الذي هو فعل المجتهد لأن الحكم بعد التأويل يضاف إلى الصيغة، فكأن النصّ ورد بهذا، وإنما قيد بقوله: من أي بهذا الحكم المشترك؛ لأن المراد ههنا هو هذا المؤول الذي بعد المشترك، وإلا فالخفي والمشكل والمجمل إذا زال خفاؤها بدليل ظني صار مؤولاً أيضًا، ولكنه من أقسام البيان، والمراد بغالب الرأي الظن الغالب، سواء حصل بخبر الواحد أو القياس أو نحوه، فلا يقال: من حيث قيل حقيقة فقط، وقيل: لا حقيقة ولا مجازا . المحشي) وإنما عد إلخ: دفع إشكال مقدر تقريره: أن المراد من المؤول يظهر بغلب الرأي، فلا يكون حينئذٍ من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة. (القمر) يضاف إلخ لأن إضافة الحكم إلى الدليل الأقوى أولى، فأثر الرأي إنما هو في إظهار المراد من المشترك، ولك أن تقول: إن إضافة الحكم بعد التأويل إلى مجرد الصيغة ممنوع، وأما إلى الصيغة بانضمام التأويل فمسلّم لكنه غير نافع، وقد يجاب عن الإشكال بأن عدّ المؤول من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة إنما هو بتبعية المشترك الذي هو من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة لا بالأصالة فتأمل. (القمر) من أقسام البيان لا من أقسام النظم صيغة ولغة. (القمر) والمراد بغالب إلخ: دفع دخل تقريره : أن المؤول قد يكون فيه الترجيح بخبر الواحد ولا يشمله تعريف المتن فليس جامعا، وحاصل الدفع: أنه ذكر الخاص وأريد العام، أو ذكر الملزوم وأريد اللازم، فالمراد بغالب إلخ. (القمر) والمراد بغالب الرأي إلخ لما كان متبادر من غالب الرأي رأي المجتهد أي اجتهاده، فيتوهم منه أن ترجيح المشترك إنما يكون باجتهاد المجتهد لا بغيره فدفع هذا بقوله : والمراد إلخ، وأراد بالرأي الظن سواء كان باجتهاد أي القياس الشرعي أو بالقرائن أو بخبر الواحد.(السنبلي) الظن الغالب فلو كان صارف اللفظ إلى بعض محتملاته قطعيًا سميناه مفسراً. (القمر) أو نحوه: كالتأمل في الصيغة كما في ثلاثة قروء. (القمر)
As for al-Mu'awwal: it is that [word] from al-mushtarak (homonym) whose one of its aspects is preponderated by dominant opinion. That is, as long as one of its two meanings has not been preponderated over the other, it is mushtarak. When one of its meanings is preponderated by the interpretation (ta'wil) of the mujtahid, that same mushtarak becomes mu'awwal. And it is counted among the divisions of the text (nazm) even though it is attained by the act of interpretation, which is the act of the mujtahid, because the ruling after interpretation is attributed to the formula (sighah), so it is as if the text has come with this. And his statement is restricted by 'from which is intended this ruling' to mushtarak because the intended here is this mu'awwal that follows mushtarak. Otherwise, al-khafi, al-mushkil, and al-mujmal, when their obscurity is removed by a speculative (zanni) proof, become mu'awwal as well, but it belongs to the divisions of bayan (clarification). What is meant by 'ghalib al-ra'y (dominant opinion)' is predominant speculation (zann ghalib), whether obtained by a solitary report (khabar wahid) or by analogy (qiyas) or similar. So it is not said... (marginal comments follow).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition, explaining the term 'mu'awwal' as used in the Hanafi textual hierarchy. The author clarifies that mu'awwal is a mushtarak (a word with multiple possible meanings) after the mujtahid's interpretation has given one meaning preponderance over others based on predominant opinion (zann ghalib). This preponderance can come from a solitary hadith, analogy, or reflection on the wording or context. The author notes that once mucategorized as mu'awwal, it is treated as part of the textual corpus (nazm) because the ruling is attributed to the wording itself, not merely the interpreter's effort. A key nuance: khafi, mushkil, and mujmal texts when clarified by a zanni proof also become mu'awwal, but they belong to the category of bayan (clarification), not primary nazm. The author gives an example: the word 'quru' in the Qur'an (three quru') is mushtarak between menstruation and purity; by examining context it becomes mu'awwal. This lesson focuses on the definition and its conditions, showing how the Hanafi tradition distinguishes categories of textual clarity.

Key Terms
المؤول (al-mu'awwal): The mushtarak (homonym) after one meaning has been given preponderance by a mujtahid's speculation (zann ghalib).
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-ra'y): Predominant opinion or dominant speculation (zann ghalib), obtained from any speculative evidence like khabar wahid, qiyas, or contextual clues.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): A word that has multiple possible meanings with no preponderance until interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the term 'ghalib al-ra'y' (predominant opinion) include in the definition of mu'awwal?
A) Only the personal ijtihad of the mujtahid without external evidence.
B) Speculative proofs such as khabar wahid, qiyas, and contextual clues.
C) Only definitive evidence from the Qur'an and Mutawatir hadith.
D) The consensus of jurists only.

Key Takeaway
Mu'awwal is a mushtarak whose meaning is chosen by predominant opinion, and in Hanafi usul it is considered part of the textual divisions (nazm) because the ruling is attributed to the sighah.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate

Al-Nass: Definition and Distinction from al-Zahir
Definition of al-Nass and its superiority over al-Zahir due to siyaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Nass in Hanafi usul, distinguish it from al-Zahir using the condition of siyaq, and apply this distinction to classify a given textual expression.

Core Idea
Al-Nass gains clarity from the speaker's intent (siyaq), not merely the wording; al-Zahir stands without siyaq.

In Hanafi usul, not every clear text is equally binding; the speaker's intention plays a crucial role. This lesson unpacks the definition of al-Nass, a text whose clarity is enhanced because the speaker specifically intended that meaning. We will contrast it with al-Zahir, which is understood from the wording regardless of intent, and see how this distinction impacts legal derivation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition of al-Nass
Read the Arabic definition: 'ما ازداد وضوحًا على الظاهر بمعنى من المتكلم لا بنفس الصيغة'. Note the two key components: increased clarity over al-Zahir, and that the additional clarity comes from the speaker's intended meaning, not from the wording itself.
Focus on 'بمعنى من المتكلم' – this is the distinct element.
2
Understand the role of siyaq
Siyaq means the speech is 'conveyed' (مسوق) for that meaning. For al-Nass, siyaq is required; for al-Zahir, it is not necessarily required. This is the primary differentiator.
The well-known view in the Hanafi school holds that siyaq is essential for al-Nass.
3
Work through the examples
Example 1: 'جاءني القوم' – this is nass for the coming of the people because the speaker intended that meaning. Example 2: 'رأيت فلانًا حين جاءني القوم' – this is nass for seeing (intended) and zahir for the coming (not intended). Practice identifying which part is nass and which is zahir.
The differing clarity affects how a ruling is derived from the text.
4
Examine the alternative view (most books)
Some earlier Hanafi scholars hold that al-Zahir is more general: it may or may not require siyaq, while al-Nass always requires it. This makes the contrast relational rather than absolute. Understand how this view broadens the scope of al-Zahir.
This does not contradict the core definition but refines the relationship.
5
Apply the distinction to a new text
Take a sentence like 'أمر الله بالعدل'. Is it nass or zahir for the obligation of justice? Consider whether the speech is 'conveyed' specifically for that ruling or if it is a general statement.
The answer may depend on the siyaq: if the context shows the speaker intended to legislate, it is nass.

Section on al-Zahir. Definition of al-Nass and its ruling. As for al-Nass, it is that which has increased clarity over al-Zahir by a meaning from the speaker, not by the wording itself; meaning that one understands from it a meaning not understood from al-Zahir because the speaker conveyed that expression for that meaning, not merely by the wording. And the well-known among the people is that for al-Nass, siyaq (context of intent) is required, while for al-Zahir, siyaq is not required, so there is a distinct difference between them. So if one says: 'The people came to me,' it is nass for the coming of the people. And if one says: 'I saw so-and-so when the people came to me,' it is nass for the seeing and zahir for the coming of the people. But it is mentioned in most books that al-Zahir is more general, whether siyaq is required or not, and al-Nass requires siyaq absolutely. And such is the case for every category above it, al-Mufassar and al-Muhkam, for some of them are more appropriate. As for al-Nass, etc.: it is derived from your saying: 'I extracted from the beast by effort exceeding its usual pace' – thus said Fakhr al-Islam. (Al-Qamar: 'by a meaning' meaning by a meaning coming from the speaker, which is the speaker's conveying of that text for that understood meaning.) (Al-Qamar: 'not in the wording itself' meaning not by a meaning that is in the wording itself.) (Al-Qamar: 'because' meaning because of a contextual clue that indicates that the speaker, etc.) (Al-Qamar: 'absence of siyaq' meaning it is not conveyed for the meaning for which it is zahir.) (Al-Qamar: 'for the coming of the people' because this statement is conveyed for it.) (Al-Qamar: 'zahir' because it is not intended by the siyaq.) (Al-Qamar: 'zahir for the coming of the people' because it is not intended by the siyaq. And if one said initially: 'The people came to me,' it would be nass for the coming of the people because it is intended by the siyaq. This is because when speech is conveyed for an intended meaning, there is increased clarity relative to what is not conveyed for; for this reason the explicit statement (ibara) of the nass is preponderant over its indication (ishara).) (Al-Sunbuli: 'in most books' i.e., of the earlier scholars, like al-Taqwim of al-Qadi Imam Abu Zayd and Usul al-Fiqh of Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr – thus it is said.) (Al-Qamar: 'more general, whether siyaq is required or not' – he said in al-Ghaya, supporting what is in most books: do you not see how Shams al-A'imma and others, when quoting parallels, included both what is conveyed and what is not conveyed? And none of the usul scholars mentioned this condition in defining al-Zahir; if it were considered, they would not have all neglected it. Know that the contrast between al-Zahir and al-Nass, according to the well-known, is real; and according to what is in most books, it is relational, taking the aspect in its meaning, according to reality, as absolute generality and specificity.) (Al-Sunbuli: 'requires' either it admits takhsis and ta'wil or not.) (Al-Qamar: 'every category above it' – for al-Mufassar, the absence of possibility of takhsis and ta'wil is required, whether it admits abrogation or not; and for al-Muhkam, the absence of any possibility of takhsis, ta'wil, and abrogation is required.)
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defines al-Nass within the Hanafi text-clarity hierarchy. The passage type is a definition (usul_definition) with commentary from various Hanafi scholars. The author first gives the core definition: al-Nass is a text whose clarity is increased over al-Zahir due to the speaker's intended meaning (ma'na min al-mutakallim), not merely from the wording itself. This means that al-Nass is understood as intended by the speaker, whereas al-Zahir is understood from the wording without requiring that the speaker specifically intended that meaning. The well-known view (mashhur) among Hanafi usul scholars is that al-Nass requires siyaq (i.e., the speech is conveyed for that meaning), while al-Zahir does not require siyaq, making them distinct. Examples are given: 'The people came to me' is nass for the coming because the statement is conveyed for that meaning; 'I saw so-and-so when the people came to me' is nass for seeing (intended) and zahir for the coming (not intended). However, most books (of earlier scholars) hold that al-Zahir is more general and may or may not require siyaq, while al-Nass always requires siyaq. This leads to a relational contrast where al-Zahir and al-Nass may overlap in some senses. The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli elaborates on the derivation of the term 'nass' from extracting something with effort, and emphasizes that the condition of siyaq is not universally required for al-Zahir. The passage also notes that this hierarchy applies to higher categories like al-Mufassar and al-Muhkam. The ruling of al-Nass is wujub al-amal (obligation to act) even though there remains a possibility of ta'wil or takhsis, but such possibilities are not based on evidence and thus do not harm the certainty of the ruling.

Key Terms
النص (al-nass): ما ازداد وضوحًا على الظاهر بمعنى من المتكلم لا بنفس الصيغة
الظاهر (al-zahir): ما يفهم منه معنى من الصيغة دون اعتبار قصد المتكلم؛ وهو أعم من أن يشترط فيه السوق أو لا
السوق (al-siyaq): كون الكلام مسوقًا للمعنى المقصود من المتكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the well-known view in Hanafi usul, what is the essential requirement for a text to be classified as al-Nass?
A) The wording must be unambiguous.
B) The text must be from the Quran or Sunnah.
C) The speaker must have conveyed the speech for that intended meaning (siyaq).
D) The text must admit of no interpretation.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nass is distinguished from al-Zahir by the presence of siyaq (speaker's intent), making it more binding in legal derivation.

Al-Mufassar: The Definitive Text in Hanafi Usul
Definition of al-Mufassar with commentary on clarity and ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Mufassar, distinguish it from al-Nass and al-Zahir, and apply the Hanafi rule that al-Mufassar is qat'i al-dalala (definitive in meaning).

Core Idea
Al-Mufassar is text so clear that no interpretation or specification can change its meaning — its ruling is certain and absolute.

This passage defines al-Mufassar, the highest level of textual clarity in the Hanafi hierarchy (after al-Muhkam). Before presenting the definition, the author recaps the status of al-Nass and al-Zahir, which admit possibilities of ta'wil and takhsis, but these do not undermine certainty because they are unsupported. Al-Mufassar elevates clarity to the point where such possibilities are blocked entirely. Understanding al-Mufassar is crucial for identifying when a text is qat'i al-dalala, binding without alternative interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Recall the hierarchy
Recognize that al-Mufassar is positioned above al-Nass and al-Zahir. Al-Nass and al-Zahir have possible interpretations, but they do not affect certainty.
Review the earlier discussion on al-Nass if needed.
2
Parse the definition
Read the Arabic: 'ما ازداد وضوحًا على النص على وجه لا يبقى معه احتمال التأويل والتخصيص'. Identify the condition: no possibility of ta'wil or takhsis remains.
Key terms: تأويل (ta'wil) = interpretation; تخصيص (takhsis) = specification.
3
Identify the two causes
Understand that this absolute clarity is achieved either by the Prophet's definitive bayan (after a mujmal statement) or by an additional word from Allah that inherently blocks ta'wil and takhsis.
The passage mentions 'ببيان النبي' or 'بإيراد الله كلمة زائدة'.
4
Derive the ruling
Since the intended meaning is certain, the ruling is wujub al-amal bihi qat'an wa yaqinan. Distinguish this from the ruling of al-Nass (which is also wujub but with possible interpretation that does not harm certainty).
The commentary stresses that possibilities in al-Nass do not harm certainty because they are baseless.

(القمر) فلا حاجة إلخ لأن التأويل هو صرف اللفظ عن الوجه الظاهر إلى خلافه، سواء كان بالتخصيص أو بالمجاز. (القمر) ولكن إلخ استدراك لدفع توهم نشأ السابق، وهو: أن النص والظاهر من إذا احتملا التأويل فصارا ظنيين. (القمر) لا تضر إلخ لكونها ناشية بغير دليل.(القمر)
أو بإيراد إلخ : معطوف على قوله ببيان إلخ (القمر) كما سيأتي: أي مثال المفسر في المتن.(القمر) وجوب العمل به قطعا ويقينا ؛ لأنه أريد به كشف لا شبهة فيه وهو القطع بالمراد. [فتح الغفار ١٣٨]
Section on al-Mufassar. Definition of al-Mufassar and its ruling. ...such that the lower is found in the higher, so there is absolute generality and specificity between them. Al-Nass and al-Zahir, and its ruling: obligation to act upon what is clear despite the possibility of interpretation that is in the realm of metaphor; i.e., the ruling of al-Nass is obligation to act upon the meaning that is clear from it, despite the possibility of interpretation that is in the realm of metaphor. And this interpretation may be within specification (takhsis) if it is general admitting specification, and may be within other than that if it is literal admitting metaphor. So there is no need to say 'on the possibility of interpretation or specification' as others mentioned. And when al-Nass admits this possibility, then al-Zahir, which is below it, is even more likely to admit it. But such possibilities do not harm the certainty. [End of al-Nass discussion.] Definition of al-Mufassar and its ruling: As for al-Mufassar, it is that which has increased clarity over al-Nass to the extent that no possibility of interpretation (ta'wil) and specification (takhsis) remains. This possibility is cut off either by an explanation (bayan) of the Prophet, if it was ambiguous (mujmal) and then a definitive explanation by his action or statement followed, so it becomes mufassar; or by Allah's introduction of an additional word that closes the door to specification and interpretation, as will come. And its ruling is obligation to act upon it. (Al-Qamar: 'It is in the realm of metaphor' i.e., it arises without evidence. With the possibility, etc., indicating that 'upon' in the author's words means 'with'.) (Al-Qamar: 'And this interpretation' etc. refutes an objection: that if al-Nass is general, it admits specification; if it is not general but specific, it admits metaphor; therefore the author must say 'on the possibility of interpretation or specification'.) (Al-Qamar: 'There is no need' because interpretation is turning the word from its apparent face to something else, whether by specification or metaphor.) (Al-Qamar: 'But' etc. is a supplement to remove a misunderstanding that arose from the preceding: that al-Nass and al-Zahir, if they admit interpretation, become zanni.) (Al-Qamar: 'Do not harm' because they arise without evidence.) (Al-Qamar: 'Or by introduction' etc. is conjuncted to 'by an explanation' etc.) (Al-Qamar: 'As will come' i.e., the example of al-Mufassar in the text.) (Al-Qamar: 'Obligation to act upon it absolutely and certainly because it aims at unveiling in which there is no doubt, and that is certainty of the intended meaning.) [Fath al-Ghaffar 138]
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines al-Mufassar, the next level in the Hanafi text-clarity hierarchy above al-Nass. The passage type is a definition (usul_definition) with commentary. The author first recaps the ruling of al-Nass and al-Zahir, emphasizing that they are subject to possible interpretation (ta'wil) or specification (takhsis), but such possibilities do not harm the certainty of the ruling because they arise without evidence. Then al-Mufassar is defined as a text that has increased clarity over al-Nass such that no possibility of ta'wil or takhsis remains. This absolute clarity is achieved in one of two ways: either (1) by a clear explanation (bayan) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that follows an ambiguous statement, such that the ambiguity is definitively removed by his action or statement; or (2) by Allah introducing an additional word that inherently blocks the door to takhsis and ta'wil. Examples are promised later. The ruling of al-Mufassar is wujub al-amal bihi qat'an wa yaqinan (obligation to act upon it absolutely and with certainty), because it reveals the intended meaning without any doubt. The commentary clarifies that the possibility of interpretation in al-Nass does not render it zanni (speculative) because such possibilities are unsupported. Al-Mufassar is thus clear beyond any figurative interpretation or specification, although it may still be subject to abrogation (naskh), as the text hints by distinguishing it from al-Muhkam which cannot be abrogated.

Key Terms
المفسر (al-mufassar): ما ازداد وضوحًا على النص على وجه لا يبقى معه احتمال التأويل والتخصيص
التأويل (al-ta'wil): صرف اللفظ عن الوجه الظاهر إلى خلافه
التخصيص (al-takhsis): تخصيص العام ببعض أفراده

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how can a text become al-Mufassar?
A) By being from the Quran.
B) By being from the Sunnah.
C) By a clear statement from the Prophet or an additional word from Allah that blocks ta'wil and takhsis.
D) By being universally accepted.

Key Takeaway
Al-Mufassar is the highest level of textual clarity in Hanafi usul, where no possibility of interpretation or specification remains, making its ruling absolutely certain.

Definition and Ruling of Al-Mufassar in Hanafi Usul
Defines al-mufassar and its legal ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mufassar, state its ruling, and distinguish it from al-nass using the Hanafi text clarity hierarchy.

Core Idea
Al-mufassar is a text so clear it excludes all possibility of interpretation or specification—its ruling is definitive certainty.

In the Hanafi legal tradition, understanding the hierarchy of textual clarity is essential for deriving rulings with precision. This lesson introduces al-mufassar, the level of textual clarity that is beyond al-nass. We will examine its definition, how it is achieved, and why its ruling is absolutely binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its position in the hierarchy
Locate the definition of al-mufassar in the passage. Note that it is placed above al-nass in clarity.
The passage states: 'ma izdad wuduhan 'ala al-nass' (increased in clarity over al-nass).
2
Understand the two ways a text becomes mufassar
The passage mentions two causes: (1) prophetic clarification (bayan) of a previously ambiguous (mujmal) text, and (2) Allah's insertion of an extra word that blocks ta'wil and takhsis.
3
Determine the ruling of al-mufassar
The passage explicitly states: 'wa hukmuhu wujub al-'amal bihi qat'an wa yaqinan' – the obligation to act upon it with certainty.
4
Distinguish al-mufassar from al-nass
Al-nass still allows some possibility of ta'wil or takhsis, while al-mufassar excludes both completely. The passage emphasizes that the author's phrase 'on probability of ta'wil' suffices, as ta'wil encompasses takhsis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المفسر

النص
تعريف المفسر وحكمه]
وأما المفسر فما ازداد وضوحًا على النص على وجه لا يبقى معه احتمال التأويل والتخصيص سواء انقطع ذلك الاحتمال ببيان النبي عليه بأن كان مجملاً فلحقه بيان قاطع بفعل النبي أو بقوله، فصار مفسراً، أو بإيراد الله تعالى كلمة زائدة ينسد بها باب التخصيص والتأويل كما سيأتي وحكمه وجوب العمل به قطعا ويقينا؛ لأنه أريد به كشف لا شبهة فيه وهو القطع بالمراد.
The definition of al-mufassar and its ruling: As for al-mufassar, it is that which has increased in clarity over al-nass to the extent that no possibility of ta'wil (interpretive diversion) or takhsis (specification) remains, whether that possibility is cut off by a statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him—by it being initially mujmal (ambiguous) and then followed by a definitive clarification by the Prophet's action or statement, so it becomes mufassar—or by Allah the Exalted's insertion of an extra word that blocks the door of takhsis and ta'wil as will come. Its ruling is the obligation to act upon it definitively and with certainty because it intends a disclosure in which there is no doubt, and that is certainty regarding the intended meaning.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines al-mufassar within the Hanafi text clarity hierarchy. Al-mufassar is a level above al-nass: it is so clear that it excludes any possibility of ta'wil (allegorical interpretation) or takhsis (specification). This clarity can be achieved through prophetic clarification—where an initially ambiguous (mujmal) statement is later explained by the Prophet's words or actions—or through Allah's own addition of a word that prevents any specification or interpretation. The ruling of al-mufassar is that it must be acted upon with certainty (qat'i), because its meaning is indisputable. The text also distinguishes al-nass (which still allows some probability of ta'wil/takhsis) from al-mufassar. The marginal commentary clarifies that the author's phrase 'on probability of ta'wil' is sufficient, as ta'wil encompasses both takhsis and metaphorical interpretation, so there is no need to separately mention takhsis.

Key Terms
المفسر (al-mufassar): ما ازداد وضوحًا على النص بحيث لا يبقى معه احتمال التأويل والتخصيص
التأويل (at-ta'wil): صرف اللفظ عن الوجه الظاهر إلى خلافه
التخصيص (at-takhsis): تخصيص العام بإخراج بعض أفراده

Key Takeaway
Al-mufassar is the highest level of textual clarity in the Hanafi hierarchy, requiring definitive action with no room for ta'wil or takhsis.

Definition and Ruling of Al-Muhkam
Definition and ruling of al-muhkam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-muhkam, distinguish its two subcategories (li-'aynihi and li-ghayrihi), and apply its ruling that it must be acted upon without probability of naskh, ta'wil, or takhsis.

Core Idea
Al-muhkam is the highest clarity level, immune from naskh either intrinsically or after revelation ceases.

In the previous lesson, you learned about al-mufassar, a text that is clarified and must be acted upon but remains open to naskh during the Prophet's lifetime. Al-muhkam represents the final stage of clarity in the Hanafi text hierarchy. This lesson will complete your understanding by defining al-muhkam, explaining its two causes of immunity from abrogation, and stating the absolute obligation to act upon it.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of al-muhkam
Al-muhkam is a text whose intended meaning is made immune from the probability of naskh (abrogation) and tabdil (alteration). The preposition 'an' implies prevention, i.e., the meaning is in a state of prevention from such probabilities.
Note the nuance: 'an' here is for prevention (imtina'), not just avoidance.
2
Identify the two causes of immunity
Immunity can be either intrinsic (li-'aynihi) — due to the text's own meaning, such as verses on tawhid and attributes — or extrinsic (li-ghayrihi) — due to the death of the Prophet, after which no further abrogation is possible.
The text calls the first 'muhkam li-'aynihi' and the second is implied as 'muhkam li-ghayrihi'.
3
Contrast al-muhkam with al-mufassar
Al-muhkam increases in clarity over al-mufassar not in wording but in having the additional attribute of being free from naskh probability. Al-mufassar is acted upon but remains theoretically abrogable during the Prophet's time.
The word 'izdada' (increased) is deliberately omitted from the definition of muhkam to emphasize that the increase is in immunity, not in linguistic clarity.
4
Apply the ruling of al-muhkam
The ruling (hukm) of al-muhkam is the obligation to act upon it with no probability of ta'wil (interpretive reinterpretation), takhsis (specification), or naskh (abrogation).
This absolute obligation applies to all muhkam texts, whether li-'aynihi or li-ghayrihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المحكم
تعريف المحكم وحكمه
على احتمال النسخ أي حكم المفسر وجوب العمل به مع احتمال أن يصير منسوخًا، وهذا في زمن النبي فأما فيما بعده فكل القرآن محكم لا يحتمل النسخ.
أي احتمال النسخ
تعريف المحكم وحكمه]
وأما المحكم : فما أحكم المراد به عن احتمال النسخ والتبديل تعدية "عن" ههنا بتضمين معنى الامتناع أي أحكم المراد به حال كونه ممتنعا عن احتمال النسخ والتبديل، سواء كان انقطاع احتمال النسخ لمعنى في ذاته كآيات التوحيد والصفات ويسمى محكما لغيره، ولم يذكر في تعريفه لفظ "ازداد" كما ويسمى لذاته، أو بوفاة النبي ذكر فيما سبق؛ تنبيهًا على أن المحكم ما ازداد وضوحًا على المفسر بشيء، وإنما ازداد عليه بقوة فيه، وهو عدم احتمال النسخ، فمراتب الظهور قد تمت على المفسر .
وحكمه وجوب العمل به من غير احتمال لا احتمال التأويل والتخصيص، ولا احتمال النسخ.
The definition of al-muhkam and its ruling: As for al-muhkam, it is that whose intended meaning is made immune from the probability of naskh (abrogation) and tabdil (alteration). The preposition 'an' here implies prevention, meaning the intended meaning is in a state of being prevented from probability of naskh and tabdil, whether the cessation of naskh probability is due to a meaning in itself—like verses of tawhid and attributes, called muhkam li-'aynihi—or due to the death of the Prophet, as mentioned earlier, alerting that al-muhkam has increased in clarity over al-mufassar by something, and that increase is the absence of naskh probability. So the levels of clarity end at al-mufassar. Its ruling is the obligation to act upon it without any probability, neither probability of ta'wil and takhsis, nor probability of naskh.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage defines al-muhkam, the highest level of clarity in the Hanafi text hierarchy. Al-muhkam is a text whose meaning is definitively protected from any possibility of abrogation (naskh) or alteration (tabdil). This immunity can be intrinsic (li-'aynihi), such as verses about Allah's oneness and attributes that cannot be abrogated by their nature, or it can be extrinsic (li-ghayrihi), occurring after the death of the Prophet because revelation has ceased and no new abrogation can occur. The text notes that the term 'izdada' (increased) was not used in the definition, signaling that the increase in clarity over al-mufassar is not in the wording but in the added attribute of immunity from naskh. The ruling of al-muhkam is that it must be acted upon absolutely, with no possibility of ta'wil, takhsis, or naskh. The marginal commentary explains that the preposition 'an' in 'an ihtimal al-naskh' is used with the sense of prevention (imtina').

Key Terms
المحكم (al-muhkam): ما أحكم المراد به عن احتمال النسخ والتبديل
النسخ (an-naskh): رفع الحكم بدليل متأخر
التبديل (at-tabdil): تغيير الحكم أو اللفظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Muhkam li-'aynihi requires ta'wil, while li-ghayrihi does not.
D) Muhkam li-'aynihi is abrogable, while li-ghayrihi is not.

Key Takeaway
Al-muhkam is the most certain text in the Hanafi hierarchy; it must be acted upon absolutely because it is immune from all probabilities of reinterpretation, specification, or abrogation.

Quranic Examples of Zahir, Nass, and Mufassar
Providing examples for textual categories from the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify Quranic verses as zahir, nass, or mufassar based on the Hanafi textual hierarchy, and explain the reasoning behind each classification.

Core Idea
A single verse can be zahir in one aspect and nass in another; mufassar removes all ambiguity.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, texts are classified by clarity. The Quran contains verses that illustrate each level. This passage from Noor al-Anwaar provides three key examples: one that is both zahir and nass, and one that is mufassar. Understanding these examples will help you distinguish between these categories and apply them in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Examples
List the three Quranic verses cited in the passage: Surah al-Baqarah 2:275, Surah an-Nisa 4:3, and Surah al-Hijr 15:30-31.
These are the core examples used by the author.
2
Classify Each Verse
For each verse, determine whether it is an example of zahir, nass, or mufassar according to the passage. Note that 2:275 is both zahir and nass, 4:3 is zahir and nass, and 15:30-31 is mufassar.
Some verses have dual classification depending on the aspect.
3
Analyze the Reasoning
For the nass classification, note the contextual purpose of the speech (e.g., refutation of polytheists, limitation of count). For mufassar, identify how the words 'all of them' and 'together' remove possibilities of takhsis and ta'wil.
Mufassar requires explicit removal of all ambiguity.
4
Distinguish Between Categories
Compare the levels: zahir allows theoretical interpretation, nass has a clear purpose but may still allow slight interpretation, mufassar admits no specification or reinterpretation.
This hierarchy is foundational for usul al-fiqh.
5
Apply to New Verses
Use the criteria from this lesson to classify other Quranic verses you encounter in fiqh texts.
Regular practice will sharpen your istinbat skills.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثال للظاهر والنص: فقال: كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا﴾ (البقرة: 275) هذا مثال الظاهر والنص، فإنه ظاهر في حق حل البيع وحرمة الربا نص في بيان التفرقة بينهما ؛ لأن الكفار كانوا يعتقدون حل الربا حتى شبهوا البيع به، فقالوا : إنما البيع مثل الربا، فرد الله عليهم، وقال: كيف يكون ذلك وأحل الله البيع وحرم الربا، ومثاله المذكور في عامة الكتب قوله تعالى: ﴿فَانْكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَه﴾ (النساء: 3) فإنه ظاهر في إباحة النكاح نص في العدد؛ لأنه سيق الكلام له كما سيأتي.
وقوله تعالى: فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ إِلَّا إِبليس (الحجر: 30-31) مثال للمفسر، فإن قوله: "فسجد" ظاهر في سجود الملائكة نص في تعظيم آدم عليه، لكنه يحتمل التخصيص أي سجود بعض الملائكة بأن يكون الملائكة عامًا مخصوص البعض، ويحتمل التأويل بأن سجدوا متفرقين أو مجتمعين فانقطع احتمال التخصيص بقوله "كلهم"، واحتمال التأويل بقوله "أجمعون"، فصار مفسرًا لا يحتمل التخصيص ولا التأويل.
The example for al-zahir and al-nass: He said: Like His statement, the Exalted: "And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury" (2:275). This is an example of both al-zahir and al-nass. It is zahir with respect to the permissibility of trade and the prohibition of usury, and nass with respect to distinguishing between them, because the disbelievers believed usury to be permissible to the extent that they compared trade to it, saying: "Trade is just like usury." So Allah refuted them, saying: "How can that be, while Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury?" Another example mentioned in most books is His statement: "Marry what seems good to you of women, two, three, or four" (4:3). It is zahir in the permissibility of marriage and nass in the number, because the speech was brought for that purpose as will come. And His statement: "So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis" (15:30-31) is an example of al-mufassar. His word "prostrated" is zahir in the prostration of the angels and nass in honoring Adam. But it could be subject to takhsis (specification) meaning some of the angels, because "angels" is a general term that can be specified, and it could be subject to ta'wil (interpretation) that they prostrated separately or collectively. Then the possibility of takhsis was cut off by His word "all of them", and the possibility of ta'wil by His word "together", so it became mufassar, not admitting takhsis or ta'wil.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage provides concrete Quranic examples to differentiate between the categories of zahir, nass, and mufassar in Hanafi usul. The first example is the verse on trade and usury (2:275). It is zahir with respect to the ruling of permissibility of trade and prohibition of usury, because the primary indication of the words 'ahalla' (has permitted) and 'harrama' (has forbidden) is to establish a ruling. However, it is nass with respect to distinguishing between trade and usury, because the context was refuting the polytheists who equated them; the purpose of the speech was specifically to show the difference. The second example (4:3) is similarly explained: the command to marry is zahir for permissibility, while the specification of numbers (two, three, four) is nass because the speech is intended to limit the count. The third example (15:30-31) illustrates mufassar. Initially, 'the angels prostrated' is zahir, but it could be specified ('some angels') or reinterpreted ('scattered'). The words 'all of them' and 'together' remove these possibilities, achieving the level of mufassar—clear and unambiguous beyond any doubt.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-zahir): A text whose meaning is apparent but still open to theoretical interpretation or specification.
النص (al-nass): A text that is clear and specific due to the purpose of the speech, but still may allow slight interpretation.
المفسر (al-mufassar): A text that is so clear that it admits no possibility of specification or reinterpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the verse (2:275) 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury', which aspect is considered nass according to the passage?
A) The permissibility of trade
B) The prohibition of usury
C) The distinction between trade and usury
D) The fact that trade is like usury

Key Takeaway
Textual clarity in Hanafi usul is layered: a single verse may combine zahir and nass, while mufassar leaves no room for specification or interpretation.

Zahir and Nass: The Trade and Usury Verse
Provides Quranic example of Zahir and Nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir and Nass by analyzing the verse on trade and usury and identifying which part is Zahir and which is Nass.

Core Idea
A verse can be Zahir in its general ruling and Nass in its specific clarification, based on the context of revelation.

In this lesson, we examine the Quranic verse on trade and usury as a classic example of how a single verse can embody two levels of textual clarity: Zahir and Nass. Understanding this distinction is fundamental to Hanafi usul, as it determines how a text can be interpreted and applied.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse
Read the verse 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury.' Note the two rulings.
2
Identify the purpose
Understand the context: the disbelievers equated trade with usury. Allah refutes this by distinguishing them.
3
Classify each ruling
The permissibility of trade is Zahir because it is clear but could be specified. The prohibition of usury and the distinction between them is Nass because the speech is specifically brought to clarify that difference.
4
Apply the definitions
Confirm that the verse is Zahir for the hukm and Nass for the distinction, using the Hanafi definitions.

المثال للظاهر والنص] :فقال: كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا هذا مثال الظاهر والنص، فإنه ظاهر في حق حل البيع وحرمة الربا نص في بيان التفرقة بينهما ؛ لأن الكفار كانوا يعتقدون حل الربا حتى شبهوا البيع به، فقالوا : إنما البيع مثل الربا، فرد الله عليهم، وقال: كيف يكون ذلك وأحل الله البيع وحرم الربا، ومثاله المذكور في عامة الكتب قوله تعالى: ﴿فَانْكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَه فإنه ظاهر في إباحة النكاح نص في العدد؛ (النساء: ٣) لأنه سيق الكلام له كما سيأتي. الظاهر والنص وقوله تعالى: فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ إِلَّا إِبليس مثال للمفسر، فإن قوله: (الحجر: ۳۱،۳۰) "فسجد" ظاهر في سجود الملائكة نص في تعظيم آدم عليه، لكنه يحتمل التخصيص أي سجود بعض الملائكة بأن يكون الملائكة عامًا مخصوص البعض، ويحتمل التأويل بأن سجدوا متفرقين أو مجتمعين فانقطع احتمال التخصيص بقوله "كلهم"، واحتمال التأويل بقوله: "أجمعون" فصار مفسرا، ولا يقال: إنه يبقى احتمال كونهم متحلّقين أو متَصَفِّفيْنَ؛ هذا الكلام لأنه لا يضر في بيان التعظيم على أنا لا ندعي أنه مفسر من جميع الوجوه، بل من بعضها، وكذا لا يقال إنه استثني فيه إبليس فكيف يصير مفسرا؛ لأن الاستثناء ليس من قبيل التخصيص، فلا يضر لكون الكلام مفسرًا على أنه استثناء منقطع، أو مبني على التغليب، وكذا لا يقال: إنه خبر لا يحتمل النسخ، فينبغي أن يكون مثالاً للمحكم؛ بقوله أجمعون وقيل: إن احتمال المجاز القطع بسبب وقوع هذا الخبر مكرر أو تكرار الخبر بنفي احتمال المجاز. (القمر) إنه يبقى فلا يكون هذا الكلام مفسراً. (القمر) لأنه إلخ دليل لقوله: لا يقال، وتوضيحه: أن هذا الاحتمال لا ينافي كون هذا الكلام مفسراً، فإن المنافي له هو احتمال ما ينافي الغرض المسوق له الكلام، وأما احتمال التفرق فهو ينافيه؛ إذ التعظيم بالسجدة متفرقين يكون أنقص من التعظيم بالسجدة مجتمعين؛ ولذا صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة الفذ بخمس وعشرين درجة، فلما كان ينافيه قطع بإقحام لفظ "أجمعون". (القمر) لا يضر بخلاف احتمال كونهم متفرقين، فإنه يضر في بيان التعظيم (المحشي) على أنا إلخ علاوة ودليل ثان لقوله: الدائر" من لا يقال إلخ. (القمر) بل من بعضها فبقاء بعض الاحتمالات لا يضر في كونه مفسراً من بعض الوجوه. (القمر) فكيف يصير إلخ لأنه احتمل التخصيص وهو الاستثناء (القمر) لأن إلخ: دليل يقال: وكذا لا يقال إلخ. ليس من قبيل إلخ لأن التخصيص ما يكون بكلام مستقل موصول والاستثناء ليس بمستقل، وما في "مسير أن التخصيص اصطلاحًا، قصر العام بكلام مستقل يقبل التعليل، ففيه أن قصر العام بالكلام المتراخي ليس بتخصيص اصطلاحًا. (القمر) لكون إلخ ولأن الاستثناء تكلم بالباقي بعد الثنيا، فكأنه ورد الحكم بالباقي من الابتداء، والمستثنى مسكوت عنه المحشي على أنه إلخ : علاوة مثل السابق. (القمر) استثناء منقطع لأن إبليس ليس من أفراد الملائكة بل من الجن فليس هذا الاستثناء بتخصيص؛ لأن التخصيص فرع دخول المستثنى في المستثنى منه . (القمر) أو مبني على التغليب: يعني أن إبليس كان جنيًا نشأ بين أظهر الملائكة، وكان معمورًاً بالألوف من الملائكة، فغلبوا عليه كذا في تفسير البيضاوي، فجعل إبليس من أفراد الملائكة، وهذا كما يقال: الشمسان أو القمران تغليبًا، فليس دخول المستثنى حقيقية في المستثنى منه، فلا يكون تخصيص. (القمر) مبني على التغليب إلخ لأنه كان عابدًا كثيرًا بل من المقربين فصار مردودًا من وقت أدم عليه . (السنبلي) وكذا لا يقال القائل: أعظم العلماء له. (القمر) إنه خبر : أي ليس بحكم فلا يحتمل النسخ، وإلا يلزم الكذب عليه تعالى (القمر)
The example for Zahir and Nass: He said: such as His statement: 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury.' This is an example of Zahir and Nass. It is Zahir regarding the permissibility of trade and the prohibition of usury, and Nass in clarifying the distinction between them, because the disbelievers used to believe usury was permissible to the extent that they compared trade to it. They said: 'Trade is just like usury.' Allah refuted them and said: 'How can that be when Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury?' And its example mentioned in most books is His statement: 'Marry what is lawful for you of women, two, three, or four.' It is Zahir in the permissibility of marriage and Nass in the number (of wives) because the speech was brought for that purpose, as will come. Zahir and Nass. And His statement: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis' is an example of Mufassar. His statement 'prostrated' is Zahir in the prostration of the angels and Nass in the veneration of Adam (peace be upon him), but it was possible of specification, i.e., prostration of some angels, making 'angels' general but specified to some, and possible of interpretation, i.e., they prostrated separately or together. So the possibility of specification was removed by His statement 'all of them', and the possibility of interpretation by His statement 'together', so it became Mufassar. And it cannot be said that there remains the possibility that they were in circles or in rows, because that does not harm in expressing veneration. Moreover, we do not claim it is Mufassar in all respects, but rather in some. Likewise, it cannot be said that Iblis is excepted, so how can it be Mufassar? Because exception is not a type of specification, so it does not harm it being Mufassar, considering it is a disconnected exception or based on preponderance. Likewise, it cannot be said that it is informative (khabar) and not susceptible to abrogation, so it should be an example of Muhkam. (Al-Qamar commentary follows).
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul categories of textual clarity: Zahir, Nass, and Mufassar. The author first gives two examples for Zahir and Nass: the verse on trade and usury, and the verse on marriage. The verse on trade is Zahir in the rulings of permissibility and prohibition, but Nass in distinguishing trade from usury because the verse was revealed in response to those who equated them. The marriage verse is Zahir in permissibility of marriage (since the command is not obligatory) and Nass in the limitation of number (two, three, four) because the speech is directed towards that limit. The commentary clarifies that 'nass' here means the word is used for its clear meaning due to the context of the verse. Then the author provides an example of Mufassar: the verse on the prostration of the angels. Initially, 'prostrated' is Zahir, and 'angels' is general. The specification that all angels prostrated is removed by 'all of them', and the interpretation of how they prostrated (separately or together) is removed by 'together'. However, the text is still not Muhkam because possibilities remain such as being in circles or rows, but these do not negate the purpose of veneration. The commentary from Al-Qamar defends why this verse is Mufassar and not Muhkam, addressing objections regarding exception of Iblis (explaining it as disconnected exception or preponderance) and noting that the verse is khabar (informative) not a legal ruling, so it is not subject to naskh, but it is still not Muhkam because it retains some interpretive possibilities. The passage teaches that Mufassar is clearer than Zahir and Nass but is not the highest level of clarity (Muhkam).

Key Terms
ظاهر (Zahir): A text that is clear in its meaning but open to possible specification or interpretation.
نص (Nass): A text that is clear and decisive in its specific meaning, such that it cannot be interpreted otherwise, having been brought for that purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, why is the verse on trade and usury considered Nass in the distinction between trade and usury?
A) Because the words 'trade' and 'usury' are clear.
B) Because the verse was revealed to refute those who equated them.
C) Because it is a legal ruling.
D) Because it uses the word 'halal' and 'haram'.

Key Takeaway
A verse can be both Zahir and Nass simultaneously, depending on the aspect being considered.

Zahir and Nass: The Marriage Verse
Provides Quranic example of Zahir and Nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Zahir and Nass in the marriage verse and explain why the limitation on the number of wives is Nass.

Core Idea
The command to marry is Zahir, but the numerical limit is Nass, because the verse was revealed to restrict pre-Islamic unlimited polygamy.

The verse 'Marry what is lawful for you of women, two, three, or four' is a classic example of Zahir and Nass. While the permissibility of marriage is clear, the specific numbers are decisive and brought to limit a previous practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse
Read the verse 'Marry what is lawful for you of women, two, three, or four.' Note the command and the number.
2
Understand the context
Pre-Islamic Arabs practiced unlimited polygamy. This verse was revealed to restrict the number to four.
3
Classify each part
The command 'marry' indicates permission (Zahir) because it is not an obligation. The restriction to two, three, or four is Nass because the verse is specifically brought for that limitation.
4
Confirm with Hanafi definitions
Zahir is clear but open to interpretation; Nass is decisive and brought for a specific purpose. The number is decisive in limiting polygamy.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Mufassar: The Prostration of Angels Verse
Provides Quranic example of Mufassar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the verse on the prostration of angels is Mufassar and not Muhkam, and identify the removal of specification and interpretation.

Core Idea
A text becomes Mufassar when potential specification and interpretation are removed by additional clarifying words, even if it remains open to minor possibilities.

The verse 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis' is a prime example of Mufassar. It is clearer than Zahir and Nass because the words 'all of them' and 'together' remove the possibilities of partial prostration or separate prostration, but it is not Muhkam because it is a report and still open to some interpretive nuances.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse
Read the verse 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis.'
2
Identify initial possibilities
Without additional words, 'the angels prostrated' could mean only some angels, or they prostrated separately. This is the Zahir level.
3
See how specification is removed
The word 'all of them' (كلهم) removes the possibility that only some prostrated. This eliminates takhsis.
4
See how interpretation is removed
The word 'together' (أجمعون) removes the possibility that they prostrated separately, i.e., it specifies the manner of prostration as collective.
5
Determine the level: Mufassar not Muhkam
Even after removing these possibilities, minor possibilities remain (e.g., being in circles or rows), but they do not affect the main purpose. The verse is Mufassar, not Muhkam, because it is a khabar (report) and Muhkam applies only to legal rulings.
