المثال للظاهر والنص] :فقال: كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَحَلَّ اللهُ الْبَيْعَ وَحَرَّمَ الرِّبا هذا مثال الظاهر والنص، فإنه ظاهر في حق حل البيع وحرمة الربا نص في بيان التفرقة بينهما ؛ لأن الكفار كانوا يعتقدون حل الربا حتى شبهوا البيع به، فقالوا : إنما البيع مثل الربا، فرد الله عليهم، وقال: كيف يكون ذلك وأحل الله البيع وحرم الربا، ومثاله المذكور في عامة الكتب قوله تعالى: ﴿فَانْكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَه فإنه ظاهر في إباحة النكاح نص في العدد؛ (النساء: ٣) لأنه سيق الكلام له كما سيأتي. الظاهر والنص وقوله تعالى: فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ إِلَّا إِبليس مثال للمفسر، فإن قوله: (الحجر: ۳۱،۳۰) "فسجد" ظاهر في سجود الملائكة نص في تعظيم آدم عليه، لكنه يحتمل التخصيص أي سجود بعض الملائكة بأن يكون الملائكة عامًا مخصوص البعض، ويحتمل التأويل بأن سجدوا متفرقين أو مجتمعين فانقطع احتمال التخصيص بقوله "كلهم"، واحتمال التأويل بقوله: "أجمعون" فصار مفسرا، ولا يقال: إنه يبقى احتمال كونهم متحلّقين أو متَصَفِّفيْنَ؛ هذا الكلام لأنه لا يضر في بيان التعظيم على أنا لا ندعي أنه مفسر من جميع الوجوه، بل من بعضها، وكذا لا يقال إنه استثني فيه إبليس فكيف يصير مفسرا؛ لأن الاستثناء ليس من قبيل التخصيص، فلا يضر لكون الكلام مفسرًا على أنه استثناء منقطع، أو مبني على التغليب، وكذا لا يقال: إنه خبر لا يحتمل النسخ، فينبغي أن يكون مثالاً للمحكم؛ بقوله أجمعون وقيل: إن احتمال المجاز القطع بسبب وقوع هذا الخبر مكرر أو تكرار الخبر بنفي احتمال المجاز. (القمر) إنه يبقى فلا يكون هذا الكلام مفسراً. (القمر) لأنه إلخ دليل لقوله: لا يقال، وتوضيحه: أن هذا الاحتمال لا ينافي كون هذا الكلام مفسراً، فإن المنافي له هو احتمال ما ينافي الغرض المسوق له الكلام، وأما احتمال التفرق فهو ينافيه؛ إذ التعظيم بالسجدة متفرقين يكون أنقص من التعظيم بالسجدة مجتمعين؛ ولذا صلاة الجماعة أفضل من صلاة الفذ بخمس وعشرين درجة، فلما كان ينافيه قطع بإقحام لفظ "أجمعون". (القمر) لا يضر بخلاف احتمال كونهم متفرقين، فإنه يضر في بيان التعظيم (المحشي) على أنا إلخ علاوة ودليل ثان لقوله: الدائر" من لا يقال إلخ. (القمر) بل من بعضها فبقاء بعض الاحتمالات لا يضر في كونه مفسراً من بعض الوجوه. (القمر) فكيف يصير إلخ لأنه احتمل التخصيص وهو الاستثناء (القمر) لأن إلخ: دليل يقال: وكذا لا يقال إلخ. ليس من قبيل إلخ لأن التخصيص ما يكون بكلام مستقل موصول والاستثناء ليس بمستقل، وما في "مسير أن التخصيص اصطلاحًا، قصر العام بكلام مستقل يقبل التعليل، ففيه أن قصر العام بالكلام المتراخي ليس بتخصيص اصطلاحًا. (القمر) لكون إلخ ولأن الاستثناء تكلم بالباقي بعد الثنيا، فكأنه ورد الحكم بالباقي من الابتداء، والمستثنى مسكوت عنه المحشي على أنه إلخ : علاوة مثل السابق. (القمر) استثناء منقطع لأن إبليس ليس من أفراد الملائكة بل من الجن فليس هذا الاستثناء بتخصيص؛ لأن التخصيص فرع دخول المستثنى في المستثنى منه . (القمر) أو مبني على التغليب: يعني أن إبليس كان جنيًا نشأ بين أظهر الملائكة، وكان معمورًاً بالألوف من الملائكة، فغلبوا عليه كذا في تفسير البيضاوي، فجعل إبليس من أفراد الملائكة، وهذا كما يقال: الشمسان أو القمران تغليبًا، فليس دخول المستثنى حقيقية في المستثنى منه، فلا يكون تخصيص. (القمر) مبني على التغليب إلخ لأنه كان عابدًا كثيرًا بل من المقربين فصار مردودًا من وقت أدم عليه . (السنبلي) وكذا لا يقال القائل: أعظم العلماء له. (القمر) إنه خبر : أي ليس بحكم فلا يحتمل النسخ، وإلا يلزم الكذب عليه تعالى (القمر)
The example for Zahir and Nass: He said: such as His statement: 'And Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury.' This is an example of Zahir and Nass. It is Zahir regarding the permissibility of trade and the prohibition of usury, and Nass in clarifying the distinction between them, because the disbelievers used to believe usury was permissible to the extent that they compared trade to it. They said: 'Trade is just like usury.' Allah refuted them and said: 'How can that be when Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury?' And its example mentioned in most books is His statement: 'Marry what is lawful for you of women, two, three, or four.' It is Zahir in the permissibility of marriage and Nass in the number (of wives) because the speech was brought for that purpose, as will come. Zahir and Nass. And His statement: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together, except Iblis' is an example of Mufassar. His statement 'prostrated' is Zahir in the prostration of the angels and Nass in the veneration of Adam (peace be upon him), but it was possible of specification, i.e., prostration of some angels, making 'angels' general but specified to some, and possible of interpretation, i.e., they prostrated separately or together. So the possibility of specification was removed by His statement 'all of them', and the possibility of interpretation by His statement 'together', so it became Mufassar. And it cannot be said that there remains the possibility that they were in circles or in rows, because that does not harm in expressing veneration. Moreover, we do not claim it is Mufassar in all respects, but rather in some. Likewise, it cannot be said that Iblis is excepted, so how can it be Mufassar? Because exception is not a type of specification, so it does not harm it being Mufassar, considering it is a disconnected exception or based on preponderance. Likewise, it cannot be said that it is informative (khabar) and not susceptible to abrogation, so it should be an example of Muhkam. (Al-Qamar commentary follows).
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul categories of textual clarity: Zahir, Nass, and Mufassar. The author first gives two examples for Zahir and Nass: the verse on trade and usury, and the verse on marriage. The verse on trade is Zahir in the rulings of permissibility and prohibition, but Nass in distinguishing trade from usury because the verse was revealed in response to those who equated them. The marriage verse is Zahir in permissibility of marriage (since the command is not obligatory) and Nass in the limitation of number (two, three, four) because the speech is directed towards that limit. The commentary clarifies that 'nass' here means the word is used for its clear meaning due to the context of the verse. Then the author provides an example of Mufassar: the verse on the prostration of the angels. Initially, 'prostrated' is Zahir, and 'angels' is general. The specification that all angels prostrated is removed by 'all of them', and the interpretation of how they prostrated (separately or together) is removed by 'together'. However, the text is still not Muhkam because possibilities remain such as being in circles or rows, but these do not negate the purpose of veneration. The commentary from Al-Qamar defends why this verse is Mufassar and not Muhkam, addressing objections regarding exception of Iblis (explaining it as disconnected exception or preponderance) and noting that the verse is khabar (informative) not a legal ruling, so it is not subject to naskh, but it is still not Muhkam because it retains some interpretive possibilities. The passage teaches that Mufassar is clearer than Zahir and Nass but is not the highest level of clarity (Muhkam).

Key Terms
مفسر (Mufassar): A text that has been clarified to remove possibilities of specification and interpretation, but not to the degree of absolute unequivocality (Muhkam).
محكم (Muhkam): A text that is absolutely clear and cannot be abrogated or reinterpreted; applies only to hukm (legal rulings), not khabar (reports).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the prostration of angels verse considered Mufassar and not Muhkam?
A) Because it contains an exception (Iblis).
B) Because it has minor remaining possibilities like arrangement in rows.
C) Because it is a report, not a legal ruling.
D) Because it uses the word 'together'.

Key Takeaway
The verse becomes Mufassar when the words 'all of them' and 'together' remove primary ambiguities, but it remains less than Muhkam because it is a report.

Muhkam: The Most Explicit Text and Its Immunity from Abrogation
Explaining the example for muhkam and preferring a hadith over a verse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a text as muhkam and explain why it is immune to both interpretation (ta'wil) and abrogation (naskh), using the example of the hadith on jihad.

Core Idea
A muhkam text is explicit, immutable, and immune to both ta'wil and naskh.

In this lesson, we explore the highest level of textual clarity in Hanafi usul: al-muhkam. Through the example of the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection', we see why a ruling with explicit perpetuity is considered muhkam, and why the verse about Allah's knowledge, though also muhkam, belongs to beliefs rather than rulings. Understanding muhkam helps us distinguish between texts that can be abrogated or reinterpreted and those that cannot.

Guided Path
1
Define muhkam
State the definition of muhkam as the most explicit text in the Hanafi hierarchy, immune to ta'wil and naskh.
Refer to the legal definition dissector for precise terms.
2
Identify the two examples
Locate the verse 'Indeed Allah is of all things Knowing' and the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection' in the passage.
Both are given as examples of muhkam.
3
Compare the examples
Explain why the author of al-Tawdih preferred the hadith: it is a ruling (hukm) of Sharia with explicit perpetuity, whereas the verse is about divine attributes (aqidah).
The hadith better illustrates muhkam in a fiqh context.
4
Examine immunity from naskh
Understand that muhkam texts cannot be abrogated because they are explicit and pertain to immutable matters, but note that the wording of a text can be abrogated while the meaning remains (e.g., abrogated Quranic verses).
Reports (akhbar) cannot be abrogated in meaning to avoid falsehood.
5
Apply the concept
Given a new text, determine if it meets the criteria for muhkam: explicit, no interpretation possible, and indicates perpetuity or an immutable matter.
Practice with examples from the practice tasks.

وقوله تعالى: وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ مثال للمحكم؛ لأنه نص في مضمونه، فلم يحتمل التأويل (الأنفال: ٧٥) والنسخ؛ إذ هو من باب العقائد في بيان التوحيد والصفات، ولما لم يكن هذا من أحكام الشرع قال صاحب التوضيح : ههنا أيضًا أن الأولى في مثال المحكم قوله عليه: "الجهاد ماض إلى يوم القيمة"؛ " لأنه من باب الأحكام، ولم يحتمل النسخ؛ لما فيه من توقيت أو تأييد ثبت نصا. لأن الخ: دليل لقوله: وكذا لا يقال . (القمر) كان محتملاً إلخ لاستقلاله؛ ويمكن أن يقال: أصل هذا الكلام أمر للملائكة بالسجود لآدم، فهو حكم يحتمل النسخ ولما وقع السجود لآدم صار خبرًا فلا يحتمل النسخ بعارض الخبرية تدبر. (القمر) وإنما ارتفع هذا إلخ لأن النسخ يكون في كلام دال على حكم من أحكام الشرع. (القمر) بعارض كونه خبرًا إلخ والحاصل أن المفسر يحتمل النسخ في نفس الأمر وإن كان هذا المثال لا يحتمله؛ لأنه من الأخبار والخبر لا يحتمل النسخ والمشايخ عبروا بقولهم: الأخبار لا يحتمل النسخ المعاني الناسخة بصيغة الأخبار؛ لأنه يؤدي إلى الكذب وظهور الغلط، وذا يستحيل على الله تعالى لا نفس الصيغة، فنفس الصيغة يحتمل النسخ وإن كان معناها محكما، فإنه يجوز أن لا يتعلق جواز الصلاة، وحرمة القراءة على الجنب، وهو المراد من نسخ اللفظ (السنبلي) ولهذا أي لكون هذا الكلام خبرًا. (القمر) لأنه من أحكام الشرع : وقوله : "كافة سد لباب التخصيص، لكنه يحتمل النسخ ؛ لكونه حكمًا شرعيًا، يقال: جاء الناس كافة أي كلها. (القمر) الأخبار: وأخبار الله تعالى لا يحتمل النسخ لتعاليه عن الكذب والغلط. (المحشي من توقيت أو تأبيد إلخ كلمة " أو " ههنا بمعنى "بل"، وإنما قلنا هذا؛ لأن في هذا القول ليس التوقيت بوقت معين بل فيه التأبيد تدبر. (القمر) أخرجه أبو داود في "سننه" عن أنس بن مالك في حديث طويل: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "الجهاد ماض مذ بعثني الله تعالى إلى أن يقاتل آخر هذه الأمة الدجال" وأخرج مسلم في "صحيحه" رقم: ۱۹۲۲، باب قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم "لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق لا يضرهم من خالفهم" عن جابر بن سمرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "لن يبرح هذا الدين قائمًا يقاتل عصابة من المسلمين حتى تقوم الساعة".
And His saying: 'Indeed Allah is of all things Knowing' is an example for muhkam; because it is explicit in its content, so it does not admit interpretation nor abrogation; since it is from the category of beliefs concerning tawhid and divine attributes. And since this is not from the rulings of Sharia, the author of al-Tawdih said: Here too the better example for muhkam is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection'; because it is from the category of rulings and does not admit abrogation due to its containing an indefinite time or eternity established by text. ... The conclusion is that mufassar is susceptible to abrogation in itself even if this example is not (due to being a report). The scholars said: reports do not admit abrogation meaning that abrogating meanings in the form of reports leads to lying and error, which is impossible for Allah, but the form itself can be abrogated. It is narrated by Abu Dawud from Anas ibn Malik in a long hadith: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Jihad continues from when Allah sent me until the last of this community fights the Dajjal.' Muslim also narrated from Jabir ibn Samurah that the Prophet said: 'This religion will always remain established, fought by a group of Muslims until the Hour is established.'
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage discusses the example for muhkam (the most clear and unchangeable text). The verse 'Indeed Allah is of all things Knowing' is presented as an example because it is a statement about divine attributes, which is explicit (nass) in its meaning, allowing no interpretation (ta'wil) and no abrogation. However, since it pertains to beliefs (aqa'id) rather than rulings (ahkam), the author of al-Tawdih preferred a different example: the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection'. This hadith is a ruling (hukm) of Sharia (because it encourages jihad) yet it cannot be abrogated because its text indicates perpetuity or indefinite continuation. The commentator then clarifies that mufassar (the previous category) is in principle susceptible to abrogation, even if the specific verse about angels is not because it became a report. Reports in the Quran can be abrogated in terms of their wording (like some verses that were recited and then removed from the Quran) but not in terms of their meaning because that would entail falsehood regarding Allah. The hadith from Abu Dawud and Muslim are cited as evidence that jihad is perpetual.

Key Terms
محكم (muḥkam): A text that is explicit, allowing neither interpretation nor abrogation
تأويل (ta’wīl): Interpretation that diverts the apparent meaning to a non-apparent meaning

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of al-Tawdih prefer the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Resurrection' as an example for muhkam over the verse 'Indeed Allah is of all things Knowing'?
A) Because the verse is ambiguous and can be interpreted.
B) Because the hadith is from the category of rulings (ahkam) and explicitly indicates perpetuity, making it a better example for muhkam.
C) Because the verse is about beliefs and cannot be abrogated, just like the hadith.
D) Because the hadith is stronger in transmission than the verse.

Key Takeaway
A muhkam text is explicit and cannot be abrogated; the best examples are rulings with explicit perpetuity, like the hadith on jihad.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy

Mufassar and Muhkam in the Hanafi Textual Hierarchy
Definitional discussion with examples and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Mufassar and Muhkam, distinguish them based on abrogation, and apply the classification to given textual examples.

Core Idea
Mufassar is clear but abrogable; Muhkam is definitive and permanent.

Understanding the Hanafi hierarchy of textual clarity is essential for deriving rulings. This lesson focuses on two high levels: Mufassar (clear but abrogable) and Muhkam (definitive and non-abrogable). We will explore their definitions, key characteristics, and why some texts serve as better examples than others, using Quranic verses and hadith as illustrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic definitions
From the passage, extract the core definitions: Mufassar is a text clear in meaning but capable of abrogation; Muhkam is definitive and immune to abrogation or reinterpretation.
Mufassar applies to rulings, Muhkam to beliefs or perpetual rulings.
2
Distinguish based on capability of abrogation
The key difference is that Mufassar can be abrogated in principle, whereas Muhkam cannot. Muhkam is eternal and not subject to naskh.
Abrogation of wording is possible for reports but not meaning.
3
Apply the classification to given examples
Practice classifying the examples: 'Fight the polytheists all together' (9:36) is Mufassar; 'So the angels prostrated' (15:30) is a report, not Mufassar; 'Allah is of all things Knowing' (8:75) is Muhkam; 'Jihad continues until Day of Judgment' is a better Muhkam example.
Al-Tawdih prefers ruling-based examples for both categories.
4
Note the role of reports vs rulings
Reports (akhbar) are not suitable for Mufassar or Muhkam definitions because abrogation does not apply to reports in the same way. Reports can have their wording abrogated but not their meaning.
This nuance prevents misclassification.
5
Recognize the best examples per scholars
The author of al-Tawdih argues that the best Mufassar example is a Sharia ruling, and the best Muhkam example is also a ruling with perpetuity, like the hadith on jihad.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on rulings over beliefs for usul examples.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المحكم
٢٤٧
المثال للظاهر والنص
لأن أصل هذا الكلام كان محتملاً للنسخ وإنما ارتفع هذا الاحتمال بعارض كونه خبرًا، فلا ضير فيه، ولهذا قال في "التوضيح": إن الأولى في مثال المفسر هو قوله
تعالى: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ كَافَةً ؛ لأنه من أحكام الشرع، بخلاف قوله تعالى:
(التوبة: ٣٦)
فَسَجَدَ الْمَلائِكَةُ فإنه من الأخبار والقصص.
(الحجر: ٣٠)
.
وقوله تعالى: وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ مثال للمحكم؛ لأنه نص في مضمونه، فلم يحتمل التأويل (الأنفال: ٧٥) والنسخ؛ إذ هو من باب العقائد في بيان التوحيد والصفات، ولما لم يكن هذا من أحكام الشرع قال صاحب التوضيح : ههنا أيضًا أن الأولى في مثال المحكم قوله علية: "الجهاد ماض إلى يوم
القيمة"؛ " لأنه من باب الأحكام، ولم يحتمل النسخ؛ لما فيه من توقيت أو تأييد ثبت نصا.
لأن الخ: دليل لقوله: وكذا لا يقال . (القمر) كان محتملاً إلخ لاستقلاله؛ ويمكن أن يقال: أصل هذا الكلام أمر للملائكة بالسجود لآدم، فهو حكم يحتمل النسخ ولما وقع السجود لآدم صار خبرًا فلا يحتمل النسخ بعارض الخبرية تدبر. (القمر) وإنما ارتفع هذا إلخ لأن النسخ يكون في كلام دال على حكم من أحكام الشرع. (القمر) بعارض كونه خبرًا إلخ والحاصل أن المفسر يحتمل النسخ في نفس الأمر وإن كان هذا المثال لا يحتمله؛ لأنه من الأخبار والخبر لا يحتمل النسخ والمشايخ عبروا بقولهم: الأخبار لا يحتمل النسخ المعاني الناسخة بصيغة الأخبار؛ لأنه يؤدي إلى الكذب وظهور الغلط، وذا يستحيل على الله تعالى لا نفس الصيغة، فنفس الصيغة يحتمل النسخ وإن كان معناها محكما، فإنه يجوز أن لا يتعلق جواز الصلاة، وحرمة القراءة على الجنب، وهو المراد من نسخ اللفظ (السنبلي) ولهذا أي لكون هذا الكلام خبرًا. (القمر) لأنه من أحكام الشرع : وقوله : "كافة سد لباب التخصيص، لكنه يحتمل النسخ ؛ لكونه حكمًا شرعيًا، يقال: جاء الناس كافة أي كلها. (القمر) الأخبار: وأخبار الله تعالى لا يحتمل النسخ لتعاليه عن الكذب والغلط. (المحشي من توقيت أو تأبيد إلخ كلمة
" أو " ههنا بمعنى "بل"، وإنما قلنا هذا؛ لأن في هذا القول ليس التوقيت بوقت معين بل فيه التأبيد تدبر. (القمر)
أخرجه أبو داود في "سننه" عن أنس بن مالك في حديث طويل: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "الجهاد ماض مذ بعثني الله تعالى إلى أن يقاتل آخر هذه الأمة الدجال" وأخرج مسلم في "صحيحه" رقم: ۱۹۲۲، باب قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم "لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق لا يضرهم من خالفهم" عن جابر بن سمرة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "لن يبرح هذا الدين قائمًا يقاتل عصابة من المسلمين حتى تقوم الساعة".
Section on Muhkam. 247. Example for Zahir and Nass. Because the origin of this speech was capable of abrogation, but this possibility was removed by the accident of it being a report, so there is no harm. For this reason the author of al-Tawdih said: The best example of Mufassar is His statement: 'And fight the polytheists all together' (al-Tawba:36) because it is from the rulings of the Sharia, unlike His statement: 'So the angels prostrated' (al-Hijr:30) which is from reports and stories. And His statement: 'And indeed Allah is of all things Knowing' (al-Anfal:75) is an example of Muhkam because it is definitive in its content, so it does not admit interpretation or abrogation; since it is from the realm of beliefs in explaining tawhid and attributes. And because this is not from the rulings of the Sharia, the author of al-Tawdih said here as well: the best example of Muhkam is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment' because it is from the category of rulings and is not capable of abrogation due to the timing or perpetuity established definitively. Because... (al-Qamar) etc. And it can be said: the origin of this speech was a command to the angels to prostrate to Adam, so it was a ruling capable of abrogation, but when the prostration occurred it became a report, so it is not capable of abrogation due to the accident of report-ness. (al-Qamar) This possibility was removed only because abrogation occurs in speech indicating a ruling from the rulings of the Sharia. (al-Qamar) The summary is that Mufassar is capable of abrogation in itself, even if this example is not capable because it is from reports, and reports do not admit abrogation. The scholars expressed: reports do not admit abrogation of the meanings that abrogate by the wording of reports, because that leads to lying and the appearance of error, which is impossible for Allah, not the wording itself. So the wording itself is capable of abrogation even if its meaning is definitive, for it is permissible that the permissibility of prayer and the prohibition of recitation for the junub are not attached, which is meant by abrogation of the wording. (al-Sanbali) And for this reason... (al-Qamar) because it is from rulings of the Sharia: and His statement 'all together' blocks the door of specification, but it is capable of abrogation because it is a Sharia ruling. It is said: 'the people came all together' meaning all of them. (al-Qamar) Reports: and the reports of Allah are not capable of abrogation because He is exalted above lying and error. (al-Muhashi) From 'timing or perpetuity' etc. the word 'or' here means 'rather', and we only say this because in this statement there is not timing by a specific time, rather there is perpetuity. (al-Qamar) Abu Dawud narrated in his Sunan from Anas ibn Malik in a long hadith: the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Jihad continues from the time Allah sent me until the last of this community fights the Dajjal.' And Muslim narrated in his Sahih (no. 1922), chapter of his statement (peace be upon him) 'A group of my community will not cease to be manifest upon the truth, not harmed by those who oppose them,' from Jabir ibn Samura from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'This religion will not cease to be established, a band of Muslims fighting until the Hour is established.'
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a definitional discussion distinguishing between Mufassar and Muhkam in the Hanafi textual clarity hierarchy. The text begins by explaining why a Quranic verse like 'Fight the polytheists all together' (9:36) is a better example of Mufassar than the story of the angels prostrating (15:30). The reason is that Mufassar applies to rulings of the Sharia, not to reports or stories, even though reports may also be clear. Then it gives an example of Muhkam: Allah's knowledge verse (8:75) is definitive in content and not open to abrogation because it deals with beliefs. However, the commentator al-Tawdih suggests that a better example of Muhkam is the hadith 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment' because it is a ruling and perpetually abrogation-free. The marginal notes (labeled 'al-Qamar' and 'al-Sanbali') clarify that the original command to angels was a ruling, but after it occurred it became a report, so abrogation no longer applies. The discussion also clarifies that the wording of a report can be abrogated even if its meaning is not, as in cases where the legal effect of a verse is changed. The hadith from Abu Dawud and Muslim is provided as textual evidence for the perpetuity of jihad.

Key Terms
المفسر (al-mufassar): A text that is clear in meaning but capable of abrogation in itself, usually from rulings of Sharia.
المحكم (al-muhkam): A text that is definitive in meaning and immune to abrogation or interpretation, typically in beliefs or perpetually applicable rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the best example of Muhkam according to the author of al-Tawdih?
A) 'And fight the polytheists all together' (9:36)
B) 'So the angels prostrated' (15:30)
C) 'And indeed Allah is of all things Knowing' (8:75)
D) 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment' (hadith)

Key Takeaway
Mufassar is clear but abrogable; Muhkam is definitive and permanent.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
8 min
The Hierarchy of Clarity and Resolving Apparent Conflicts
Explains hierarchy and conflict resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of hierarchy (Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, Muhkam) to resolve apparent conflicts between Quranic verses and identify which text is given precedence.

Core Idea
In apparent conflict, the clearer text (Nass) overrides the less clear (Zahir) — there is no real contradiction.

This passage presents a foundational usul rule: the four levels of textual clarity in the Hanafi school are all certain in their authority, but they differ in explicitness. When two texts seem to conflict, the lower level is interpreted in light of the higher. The 'conflict' is only apparent, not real, because the higher text contextualizes and restricts the lower. A concrete example from the Quran on marriage illustrates how a general permission is limited by a specific numerical limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Levels
Locate the four terms: Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, Muhkam. Note their order from lowest to highest in clarity.
All are considered qat'i (certain) in authority, but the difference is in explicitness of meaning.
2
State the Rule for Conflict
The passage says: in a conflict, the higher level is acted upon and the lower is abandoned. This applies to any pair of adjacent levels.
This is an example of al-ta'arud al-suri (apparent conflict), not real contradiction.
3
Distinguish Apparent vs Real Conflict
Real conflict (ta'arud haqiqi) occurs when two proofs are equal and contradictory; here the levels are unequal, so conflict is resolvable.
Understanding this prevents the mistaken belief that the Quran contradicts itself.
4
Work Through the Example
Take verse 4:24 (general permission to marry beyond prohibited categories) as Zahir, and verse 4:3 (limit of four) as Nass. Apply the rule: Nass overrides Zahir, so marriage beyond four is not permitted.
Also consider the alternative interpretation regarding dowry: 4:24 as Nass on dowry, 4:3 as Zahir silent on dowry.
5
Extend the Rule to Higher Levels
The same hierarchy applies upward: Nass over Mufassar, Mufassar over Muhkam. Each level clarifies and restricts the lower.
This hierarchy is a key tool for Hanafi istinbat (derivation).

Source Text

(النساء: ٢٤)
مثال تعارض الظاهر والنص: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُمْ مَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكُمْ أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ﴾ مع قوله تعالى: ﴿فَانْكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعَ ، فإن الأول ظاهر (النساء: ٣) في حل جمع المحللات من غير قصر على الأربعة، فينبغي أن تحل الزائدة عليها، والثاني نص في أنه لا يجوز التعدي عن الأربعة؛ لأنه سيق لأجل العدد، فتعارض بينهما، فترجح نص ويقتصر عليها، وقيل: الأول نص في حق اشتراط المهر، والثاني ظاهر في عدم اشتراطه؛ لأنه ساكت عن ذكره ومطلق عنه، فتعارض بينهما فيترجح النص ويجب المال.
ليصير إلخ اللام للعاقبة أي عاقبة التفاوت وفائدته أن يصير إلخ كذا قيل. (القمر)
بين
هذه الأربعة أي الظاهر والنص والمفسر والمحكم. (القمر) فيعمل إلخ لأن العمل بالأوضح والأقوى أولى وأحرى (القمر)
أي المهر في النكاح
هذا التعارض: استدراك لدفع توهم نشأ من الكلام السابق، وهو أن التعارض بين الظاهر والنص، وبين النص
والمفسر، وبين المفسر والمحكم تعارض حقيقي. (القمر) الصوري: أي من حيث النفي والإثبات.(القمر) وههنا ليس كذلك فإن الظاهر أدنى من النص والنص من المفسر والمفسر من المحكم. (القمر)
ما وراء ذلكم إلخ أي ما وراء المحرمات المذكورة في الآية سابقا، لأن تبتغوا إلخ. (القمر)
نص في حق إلخ لأن الأول سيق لبيان اشتراط المهر. (القمر) لأنه : أي لأن الثاني ساكت عن ذكر المهر.
And the difference appears at the time of conflict, so that the lower is abandoned in favor of the higher. Meaning: the difference among these four does not appear in terms of probability and certainty because all are certain; rather, the difference appears at the time of conflict. So the higher is acted upon, not the lower. If there is a conflict between Zahir and Nass, Nass is acted upon. If there is a conflict between Nass and Mufassar, Mufassar is acted upon. If there is a conflict between Mufassar and Muhkam, Muhkam is acted upon. But this conflict is only apparent conflict, not real, because real conflict is the contradiction between two proofs equally, with no preponderance of one over the other, and here it is not so. (al-Nisa: 24) Example of conflict between Zahir and Nass: His statement 'And permitted to you are what is beyond that, that you seek with your wealth' (al-Nisa:24) along with His statement 'Then marry what is pleasing to you of women, two and three and four' (al-Nisa:3). The first is Zahir in permitting gathering of women without restriction to four, so additional women should be allowed. The second is Nass in that exceeding four is not permissible because it was brought for the number. So there is conflict between them, so the Nass is preponderated and one restricts to four. And it was said: The first is Nass regarding the requirement of the dowry, and the second is Zahir regarding not requiring it because it is silent about it and absolute. So there is conflict between them, so the Nass is preponderated and wealth is obligatory. 'So that it becomes' etc.: the lam is for consequence, i.e., the consequence of the difference and its benefit. (al-Qamar) 'Between these four' i.e., Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, and Muhkam. (al-Qamar) 'So the higher is acted upon' because acting upon the clearer and stronger is more appropriate and fitting. (al-Qamar) 'This conflict': an explanatory addition to repel a misunderstanding arising from the previous speech, that the conflict between Zahir and Nass, and between Nass and Mufassar, and between Mufassar and Muhkam is real conflict. (al-Qamar) 'Apparent' i.e., in terms of negation and affirmation. (al-Qamar) And here it is not so, because Zahir is lower than Nass, Nass lower than Mufassar, Mufassar lower than Muhkam. (al-Qamar) 'What is beyond that' i.e., beyond the prohibitions mentioned earlier in the verse. (al-Qamar) 'Nass regarding' because the first was brought to explain the requirement of dowry. (al-Qamar) 'Because' i.e., the second is silent about mentioning the dowry.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage states a foundational usul rule: the four levels of textual clarity (Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, Muhkam) are all certain (qat'i) in their authority, but they differ in explicitness. The difference only becomes operative when two texts appear to conflict. In such a case, the higher level is given precedence and the lower is set aside. The conflict is only apparent, not real, because the lower text is interpreted in light of the higher. A concrete example is given from Quranic verses on marriage. One verse (4:24) appears to permit marrying any number of women beyond the prohibited categories, which is Zahir (apparent) in allowing polygamy without numerical limit. The other verse (4:3) explicitly limits marriage to two, three, or four, making it Nass (explicit) on the number. The Nass overrides the Zahir, so marriage beyond four is not permitted. Another interpretation offered is regarding the dowry: the first verse is Nass (explicit) on requiring a dowry, while the second is Zahir (silent) on dowry, so the first prevails and dowry is obligatory. The marginal glosses clarify that 'apparent conflict' means the texts seem contradictory but in reality one is stronger, so it's not a true contradiction where both are equal.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-zahir): A text that is clear in meaning but open to interpretation or specification; lower in clarity than Nass.
النص (al-nass): A text that is explicit about a ruling and usually brought for that purpose, higher than Zahir.
التعارض الصوري (al-ta'arud al-suri): An apparent conflict that is resolved by prioritizing one text over another due to differing clarity levels.
المفسر (al-mufassar): A text that is explained or detailed, more explicit than Nass.
المحكم (al-muhkam): A text that is definitive and unambiguous, highest level.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct course of action when a text classified as Zahir conflicts with a text classified as Nass?
A) Both texts are considered abrogated
B) The Zahir is given precedence because it is more general
C) The Nass is given precedence because it is higher in clarity
D) The conflict is real and both are suspended

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, texts are ranked by clarity; when they appear to conflict, the higher-ranking text overrides the lower, resolving the apparent contradiction.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
10 min
The Hierarchy of Textual Clarity: Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, Muhkam
Explaining strength hierarchy and apparent conflict resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, and Muhkam, and apply the Hanafi rule of resolving apparent textual conflicts by preponderating the higher level.

Core Idea
When texts appear to conflict, the higher clarity level governs — this is ta'arud suri, not real contradiction.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not all clear texts are equal. This lesson introduces the four-tier hierarchy and the principle that apparent conflicts are resolved by favoring the higher level, without the need for abrogation or abandoning one text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
Name the four levels of textual clarity: al-Zahir, al-Nass, al-Mufassar, al-Muhkam. Understand that all are qat'i in their own right.
Each level represents increasing explicitness and resistance to interpretation.
2
Distinguish apparent from real conflict
Real conflict (ta'arud haqiqi) involves two equal proofs that cannot be reconciled. Apparent conflict (ta'arud suri) occurs when one text is lower in clarity and thus gives way to a higher one.
The passage emphasizes that the four texts are not truly contradictory; their different ranks make the conflict only apparent.
3
Learn the preponderance rule
When two texts appear to conflict, the higher-ranked text (Muhkam > Mufassar > Nass > Zahir) is acted upon, and the lower is set aside (though still valid in other contexts).
This is not abrogation (naskh); the lower text remains applicable where no higher text exists.
4
Examine the Quranic example
Compare Quran 4:24 (Zahir in permitting unlimited marriages) with 4:3 (Nass in limiting to four). The second text preponderates because it is more explicit about the number.
The analysis shows how the same verse can be classified differently depending on which aspect is examined (dowry vs. number).
5
Apply to hadith and fiqh examples
The mustahadah hadiths illustrate Nass vs. Mufassar, and the mut'ah marriage example shows how a Nass term ('married') is overridden by a Mufassar term ('to a month').
These examples demonstrate the practical operation of the hierarchy in deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبحث المحكم
المثال للظاهر والنص
ويظهر التفاوت عند التعارض ليصير الأدنى متروكا بالأعلى يعني لا يظهر التفاوت بين هذه الأربعة في الظنية والقطعية؛ لأن كلها ،قطعية وإنما يظهر التفاوت عند التعارض، فيعمل بالأعلى دون الأدنى، فإذا تعارض بين الظاهر والنص يعمل بالنص، وإذا تعارض بين النص والمفسر يعمل بالمفسر، وإذا تعارض بين المفسر والمحكم يعمل بالمحكم، ولكن هذا التعارض إنما هو التعارض الصوري لا الحقيقي؛ لأن التعارض الحقيقي هو التضاد بين الحجتين على السواء لا مزيد لأحدهما، وههنا ليس كذلك.
(النساء: ٢٤)
مثال تعارض الظاهر والنص: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُحِلَّ لَكُمْ مَا وَرَاءَ ذَلِكُمْ أَنْ تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُمْ﴾ مع قوله تعالى: ﴿فَانْكِحُوا مَا طَابَ لَكُمْ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ مَثْنَى وَثُلاثَ وَرُبَاعِ﴾، فإن الأول ظاهر (النساء: ٣) في حل جمع المحللات من غير قصر على الأربعة، فينبغي أن تحل الزائدة عليها، والثاني نص في أنه لا يجوز التعدي عن الأربعة؛ لأنه سيق لأجل العدد، فتعارض بينهما، فترجح الثاني ويقتصر عليها، وقيل: الأول نص في حق اشتراط المهر، والثاني ظاهر في عدم اشتراطه؛ لأنه ساكت عن ذكره ومطلق عنه، فتعارض بينهما فيترجح النص ويجب المال.
ليصير إلخ اللام للعاقبة أي عاقبة التفاوت وفائدته أن يصير إلخ كذا قيل. (القمر)
الأربعة
بين
هذه الأربعة أي الظاهر والنص والمفسر والمحكم. (القمر) فيعمل إلخ لأن العمل بالأوضح والأقوى أولى وأحرى (القمر)
أي المهر في النكاح
هذا التعارض: استدراك لدفع توهم نشأ من الكلام السابق، وهو أن التعارض بين الظاهر والنص، وبين النص والمفسر، وبين المفسر والمحكم تعارض حقيقي. (القمر) الصوري: أي من حيث النفي والإثبات.(القمر) وههنا ليس كذلك فإن الظاهر أدنى من النص والنص من المفسر والمفسر من المحكم. (القمر)
ما وراء ذلكم إلخ أي ما وراء المحرمات المذكورة في الآية سابقا، لأن تبتغوا إلخ. (القمر)
نص في حق إلخ لأن الأول سيق لبيان اشتراط المهر. (القمر) لأنه : أي لأن الثاني ساكت عن ذكر المهر.

ومثال تعارض النص مع المفسر قوله عليه: "المستحاضة تتوضأ لكل صلاة" مع قوله عليه: "المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة"، فإن الأول نص يقتضي الوضوء الجديد لكل صلاة أداءً كان أو قضاءً فرضًا كان أو نفلاً، لكنه يحتمل تأويل أن يكون اللام بمعنى الوقت فيكفي الوضوء الواحد في كل وقت، فتؤدي به ما شاءت من فرض ونفل والثاني مفسر لا يحتمل التأويل لوجدان لفظ الوقت فيه صريحًا، فإذا تعارض بينهما يصار إلى ترجيح المفسر فيكفي الوضوء الواحد في كل وقت صلاة مرة واحدة والشافعي لله لم يتنبه بهذا، فعمل بالحديث الأول.
ومثال تعارض النص إلخ ومثاله من مسائل الفقه ما قال علماؤنا فيمن تزوج امرأة إلى شهر أنه متعة لا نكاح؛ لأن قوله تزوجت نص في النكاح، ولكن احتمال المتعة فيه قائم، وقوله: "إلى شهر" مفسر في المتعة ليس فيه احتمال النكاح، فإن النكاح لا يحتمل التوقيت بحال، فإذا اجتمعا في الكلام ترجح المفسر، ويحمل النص عليه فكان متعة لا نكاحا، كذا ذكر "شمس الأئمة" ويأتي هذا شمس الأئمة" ويأتي هذا في المتن أيضًا. (السنبلي)
جده
ثابت المستحاضة إلخ روى الترمذي عن عدي بن تدع الصلاة أيام أقرائها التي كانت تحيض فيها، ثم تغتسل وتتوضأ عند كل صلاة وتصوم وتصلي". (القمر) بمعنى الوقت كما في قوله : آتيك" لصلاة الظهر" أي وقت صلاة الظهر كذا في "الهداية وأورد أن اللام حرف والوقت اسم واستعارة الحرف للاسم لا يصح؛ الصواب أن يقال: إن الأول يحتمل التأويل بأن يكون المضاف أي لفظ الوقت محذوفًا فتدبر. (القمر)
عن أبيه عن عن النبي أنه قال في المستحاضة:
أخرجه الترمذي في "جامعه" رقم: ۱۲٦، باب ما جاء أن المستحاضة تتوضاً لكل صلاة ، وابن ماجة رقم: ٦٢٥ ، باب ما جاء في المستحاضة التي قد عدت أيام أقرائها قبل أن يستمر بها الدم، عن عدي بن ثابت عن أبيه عن جده عن النبي أنه قال في المستحاضة: تدع الصلاة أيام أقرائها التي كانت تحيض فيها، ثم تغتسل وتتوضأ عند كل صلاة وتصوم وتصلي، وأخرج ابن حبان في صحيحه رقم: ۱۳۵۵ ، ۱۸۹/٤ ، عن عائشة قالت: سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن المستحاضة فقال: تدع الصلاة أيامها ثم تغتسل غسلاً واحدًا، ثم تتوضأ عند كل صلاة، والكل ضعيف. [إشراق الأبصار ٩] روى أبو حنيفة عن هشام بن عروة عن أبيه عن عائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لفاطمة بنت أبي جيش: توضئي لوقت كل صلاة، وذكر سبط ابن الجوزي أن الإمام أبا حنيفة رواه ، وذكره محمد في الأصل مفصلا. (إشراق الأبصار)
Section on al-Muhkam
Example for al-Zahir and al-Nass
And the distinction appears at the time of conflict, so that the lower is left for the higher. That is, the distinction does not appear between these four in terms of probability and certainty, because all are certain. Rather, the distinction appears at the time of conflict, so the higher is acted upon, not the lower. So if there is conflict between al-Zahir and al-Nass, one acts by al-Nass; if between al-Nass and al-Mufassar, by al-Mufassar; if between al-Mufassar and al-Muhkam, by al-Muhkam. But this conflict is only apparent conflict, not real, because real conflict is contradiction between two proofs equally with no advantage for one of them, and here it is not so.

Example of conflict between al-Zahir and al-Nass: His statement the Exalted: “And lawful to you are what is beyond that, that you seek with your wealth” [4:24] with His statement: “So marry what is good for you of women, two, three, or four” [4:3]. The first is Zahir regarding the permissibility of gathering those made lawful without restriction to four, so the additional ones should be lawful. The second is Nass that it is not permissible to exceed four, because it was brought for the number. So they conflict, and the second is preponderated and one restricts to them. And it is said: the first is Nass regarding the condition of the dowry, and the second is Zahir regarding its absence of condition, because it is silent about its mention and absolute about it. So they conflict, and al-Nass is preponderated and the wealth is obligatory.
... [additional commentary and examples follow] ...
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explains the hierarchy of textual clarity and how apparent conflicts are resolved. The author distinguishes four levels: Zahir (clear but open to interpretation), Nass (explicit), Mufassar (detailed), and Muhkam (definitive). All are considered certain (qat'i) in their own right, but when they appear to conflict, the higher level takes precedence. This is called apparent conflict (ta'arud suri) because the lower text is not truly contradictory; rather, it is at a lower level of clarity. The Quranic example compares the verse allowing marriage beyond the prohibited categories (Zahir) with the verse limiting to four (Nass). The second is Nass because it specifies a number, so it preponderates. Another example involves hadith on the mustahadah: one says 'perform wudu for every prayer' (Nass, but could be interpreted as 'for the time of every prayer'), while the other explicitly says 'for the time of every prayer' (Mufassar). The Mufassar is clearer, so wudu once per time suffices. A fiqh example: marrying a woman 'until a month' is mut'ah, not nikah, because 'married' is Nass for nikah but the term 'until a month' is Mufassar for mut'ah, which preponderates. The commentary emphasizes that this hierarchy is unique to Hanafi usul and critical for resolving textual conflicts.

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-zahir): A text that is clear in meaning but open to interpretation or specification.
النص (al-nass): A text that is explicit and unambiguous, leaving no room for interpretation in its immediate meaning.
المفسر (al-mufassar): A text that is detailed and clearly explained, with no possibility of interpretation to the contrary.
المحكم (al-muhkam): A definitive text that cannot be abrogated or subject to any reinterpretation.
التعارض الصوري (al-ta'arud al-suri): An apparent conflict between two texts where one is at a higher clarity level, making the conflict resolvable by preponderating the higher.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi hierarchy, when the hadith 'The mustahadah performs wudu for every prayer' appears to conflict with 'The mustahadah performs wudu for the time of every prayer', which category does the second hadith belong to, and why does it preponderate?
A) It is Nass, because it explicitly states wudu for every prayer time.
B) It is Mufassar, because it contains the explicit word 'time' leaving no room for interpretation.
C) It is Zahir, because it is clear but could be interpreted differently.
D) It is Muhkam, because it cannot be abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi textual clarity hierarchy (Zahir, Nass, Mufassar, Muhkam) resolves apparent contradictions by preponderating the higher level, ensuring coherent legal derivation without resorting to abrogation.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
8 min
Preference Among Nass, Mufassar, and Muhkam in Hanafi Usul
Illustrating preference rules among textual categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify texts as nass, mufassar, or muhkam and apply the Hanafi preference rule when they conflict.

Core Idea
When nass and mufassar conflict, prefer mufassar; when mufassar and muhkam conflict, prefer muhkam.

In Hanafi usul, not all clear texts are equally clear. The hierarchy from least to most explicit is nass, mufassar, muhkam. This lesson works through two key examples—the mustahadah hadith and the marriage contract—to show how these categories interact and which text prevails when they conflict. You will also see the practical difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the mustahadah's wudu.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three clarity levels
nass: susceptible to interpretation (ta'wil). mufassar: explicit, no interpretation except abrogation. muhkam: definitive, cannot be abrogated. These are the Hanafi categories for textual clarity.
2
Work through the mustahadah example
The hadith says 'wudu for every prayer' (nass, ambiguous) and 'wudu for the time of every prayer' (mufassar, explicit). Identify why the mufassar is preferred and what ruling results.
The lam in 'li kulli salat' can mean 'for' or 'at the time of'; the mufassar removes this ambiguity.
3
Work through the marriage example
'I married you until a month' – 'married' is nass for marriage but can imply mut'ah; 'until a month' is mufassar for mut'ah. Apply the preference rule and note Zufar's dissent.
Zufar held the condition invalid, preserving the marriage; Hanafis rule mut'ah (void).
4
Analyze the mufassar vs. muhkam conflict
Quran 65:2 (call two just witnesses) is mufassar for accepting testimony after repentance; Quran 24:4 (never accept) is muhkam. The muhkam prevails because it is absolute and cannot be abrogated.
The objection by al-Hissami is that 65:2 is not fully mufassar; the Hanafi response is that it is mufassar for acceptance specifically.
5
Review the objection and response
Al-Hissami argues the verse is not mufassar due to other possibilities (obligation vs. recommendation, inclusion of blind/slaves). The answer: it is mufassar only for acceptance, and the absolute is restricted to perfect witnesses.
Also, there is a claim of no conflict; but even if conflict exists, the muhkam's explicit wording outweighs the mufassar's indication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثال تعارض النص مع المفسر قوله عليه: "المستحاضة تتوضأ لكل صلاة" وقوله عليه: "المستحاضة تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة"، فإن الأول نص يقتضي الوضوء الجديد لكل صلاة أداءً كان أو قضاءً فرضًا كان أو نفلاً، لكنه يحتمل تأويل أن يكون اللام بمعنى الوقت فيكفي الوضوء الواحد في كل وقت، فتؤدي به ما شاءت من فرض ونفل والثاني مفسر لا يحتمل التأويل لوجدان لفظ الوقت فيه صريحًا، فإذا تعارض بينهما يصار إلى ترجيح المفسر فيكفي الوضوء الواحد في كل وقت صلاة مرة واحدة. والشافعي رضي الله عنه لم يتنبه بهذا، فعمل بالحديث الأول.
ومثال تعارض النص مع المفسر من مسائل الفقه ما قال علماؤنا فيمن تزوج امرأة إلى شهر أنه متعة لا نكاح؛ لأن قوله "تزوجت" نص في النكاح، ولكن احتمال المتعة فيه قائم، وقوله "إلى شهر" مفسر في المتعة ليس فيه احتمال النكاح، فإن النكاح لا يحتمل التوقيت بحال، فإذا اجتمعا في الكلام ترجح المفسر، ويحمل النص عليه فكان متعة لا نكاحاً، كذا ذكر شمس الأئمة ويأتي هذا في المتن أيضًا.
ومثال تعارض المفسر مع المحكم قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾ مع قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً أَبَدًا﴾، فإن الأول مفسر يقتضي قبول شهادة المحدودين في القذف بعد التوبة؛ لأنهما صارا عدلين حينئذ، والثاني محكم يقتضي عدم قبولها؛ لوجود التأبيد فيه صريحًا، فإذا تعارض بينهما يعمل على المحكم هكذا في كتب الأصول.
ثم أن المصنف ذكر مثالاً لتعارض النص مع المفسر على سبيل التفريع. فقال: حتى قلنا: إنه إذا تزوج امرأة إلى شهر أنه يكون متعة يريد أن قوله: "تزوج" نص في النكاح.
فإن الأول مفسر إلخ أورد شارح الحسامي أنا لا نسلم أن الأول مفسر؛ لأن المفسر ما لا يحتمل شيئاً سوى مدلوله إلا النسخ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾ يحتمل الإيجاب والندب، ويتناول بإطلاقه الأعمى والعبيد، وهما ليسا بمرادين إجماعًا، فكيف يسمى مفسرًا مع هذه الاحتمالات. وأجيب بأن الغرض أن الأول مفسر في القبول، فلا يضره هذه الاحتمالات، ولا يتناول الأعمى والعبيد لانصراف المطلق إلى الكمال ولا كمال لهما.
فإذا تعارض بينهما إلخ فيه أنه لا تعارض؛ لأن حكم الأول الإشهاد وحكم الثاني عدم قبول الشهادة عند الأداء، وليس القبول لازماً للإشهاد؛ ألا ترى أن إشهاد المحدودين في القذف والأعمى صحيح حتى ينعقد النكاح بشهادتهم، ولا يقبل شهادتهم عند الأداء، ولو سلمنا أن القبول لازم للإشهاد فالأول يدل على قبول شهادة المحدودين في القذف بطريق الإشارة، والثاني يدل على عدم قبولها بالعبارة والعبارة تترجح على الإشارة فصار الترجيح بهذا الاعتبار لا باعتبار كون الثاني محكماً والأول مفسراً تدبر.
أنه يكون متعة: خلافاً لزفر رحمه الله فإنه يقول: إن التوقيت إلى شهر باطل، والنكاح يكون صحيحاً؛ لأن النكاح لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة بل تبطل الشروط.
أنه يكون متعة: لا نكاح؛ لأن التزوج نص في النكاح وإن كان محتملاً أن يراد به المتعة مجازاً وقوله: "إلى شهر" مفسر في المتعة ليس فيه احتمال النكاح؛ إذ النكاح لا يحتمل التوقيت بحال، وإذا اجتمعا رجحنا المفسر، وحملنا النص عليه.
Example of conflict between the nass and the mufassar: His saying, peace be upon him: 'The mustahadah performs ablution for every prayer' and His saying, peace be upon him: 'The mustahadah performs ablution for the time of every prayer.' The first is a nass that necessitates a new ablution for every prayer, whether performed on time or as make-up, obligatory or supererogatory, but it is subject to interpretation that the lam might mean 'time' so one ablution suffices for each time, allowing her to perform whatever obligatory and supererogatory prayers she wishes. The second is mufassar, not subject to interpretation because the word 'time' is explicit in it. So when they conflict, preference is given to the mufassar, and one ablution suffices for each prayer time once. Al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him, did not notice this and acted upon the first hadith. Another example of conflict between nass and mufassar from fiqh issues is what our scholars said about one who marries a woman until a month: that it is mut'ah (temporary marriage) and not a valid marriage; because his saying 'I married' is nass for marriage, but the possibility of mut'ah exists in it, while his saying 'until a month' is mufassar for mut'ah, with no possibility of marriage in it, because marriage cannot be time-limited at all. So when both are joined in speech, the mufassar is given preference and the nass is interpreted accordingly, thus it is mut'ah not marriage. So mentioned Shams al-A'imma, and this will come in the text as well. Example of conflict between mufassar and muhkam: Allah's saying: 'And call to witness two just men among you' (At-Talaq 65:2) with His saying: 'And never accept their testimony again' (An-Nur 24:4). The first is mufassar requiring acceptance of the testimony of those punished for false accusation (qadhf) after repentance because they have become just then; the second is muhkam requiring non-acceptance due to the explicit word 'forever' in it. So when they conflict, the muhkam is acted upon, as recorded in books of usul. Then the author gave an example of conflict between nass and mufassar by way of branching. He said: Even we said: If a man marries a woman until a month, it is mut'ah. He intends that his saying 'married' is nass for marriage. The first is mufassar etc. The commentator al-Hissami objected: We do not accept that the first is mufassar, because mufassar is that which does not accept anything other than its denotation except abrogation, and Allah's saying 'And call to witness two just men among you' accepts obligation and recommendation and includes blind and slaves generally, though they are not intended by consensus, so how can it be called mufassar with these possibilities? It was answered: The aim is that the first is mufassar regarding acceptance, so these possibilities do not harm it, and it does not include the blind and slaves because the absolute is restricted to perfection and they have no perfection. Concerning 'when they conflict', there is no conflict because the ruling of the first is testimony and the ruling of the second is non-acceptance of testimony at the time of performance, and acceptance is not necessary for testimony; do you not see that testimony of those punished for qadhf and of a blind person is valid such that marriage is contracted through their testimony, while their testimony is not accepted at the time of performance? And if we accept that acceptance is necessary for testimony, then the first indicates acceptance of the testimony of those punished for qadhf by way of indication, and the second indicates its non-acceptance by explicit wording, and wording is given preference over indication, so the preference is from this consideration, not because the second is muhkam and the first is mufassar. Reflect. It is mut'ah, contrary to Zufar, may Allah have mercy on him, who says that the time limit to a month is void and the marriage is valid because marriage is not invalidated by invalid conditions; rather the conditions are invalid. It is mut'ah, not marriage, because 'married' is nass for marriage although it is possible to intend mut'ah figuratively, while 'until a month' is mufassar for mut'ah with no possibility of marriage; since marriage cannot be time-limited at all, and when both are combined we give preference to the mufassar and interpret the nass accordingly.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of how Hanafi usul handles conflicts between different categories of textual clarity: nass, mufassar, and muhkam. The author provides two main examples. First, between nass and mufassar: the hadith about the mustahadah. The nass (general command to do wudu for every prayer) is ambiguous because 'to' could mean 'for' or 'at the time of', while the mufassar explicitly mentions 'time', removing the ambiguity. Thus the mufassar is preferred, allowing one wudu per prayer time. The marriage example further illustrates: 'I married' (nass) can imply mut'ah, but 'until a month' (mufassar) clearly indicates mut'ah, so the contract is ruled mut'ah, not valid marriage. Second, between mufassar and muhkam: the Quranic verses. The mufassar (call two just witnesses) seems to accept the testimony of repentant qadhf punishers, but the muhkam (never accept their testimony) is absolute and cannot be interpreted away, so the muhkam prevails. The passage then addresses objections: some argued the verse is not mufassar due to other possibilities, but the response is that it is mufassar for acceptance specifically. Also argued there is no conflict because the rulings are different; but even if there were, the muhkam's explicit wording outweighs the mufassar's indication. Finally, the marriage example is defended against Zufar's view. Teachers should emphasize that this hierarchy (nass < mufassar < muhkam) is a key Hanafi principle for resolving textual conflicts.

Key Terms
نص (nass): A text that indicates a specific meaning but is susceptible to interpretation (ta'wil) via possible figurative or extended meanings.
مفسر (mufassar): A text that is explicit and does not admit any interpretation other than its literal meaning, except abrogation. It is clearer than nass.
محكم (muhkam): A text that is definitive and cannot be abrogated; it is the highest level of clarity.
متعة (mut'ah): Temporary marriage; a marriage contract with a fixed time limit, which is prohibited in Sunni Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul principle, when a nass text conflicts with a mufassar text, which is preferred and why?
A) The nass, because it is more general.
B) The mufassar, because it is more explicit and not open to interpretation.
C) Both are equal, so they are reconciled.
D) The muhkam, because it is the highest level.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi textual hierarchy (nass < mufassar < muhkam) determines which text prevails when they conflict; the more explicit text is given preference.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy

Definition and Ruling of al-Khafi (The Hidden) in Hanafi Usul
Defining al-Khafi and its ruling as a category of hiddenness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Khafi, identify its condition (accidental cause outside the wording), and apply its ruling (investigation for increase or decrease) to a textual example.

Core Idea
Al-Khafi is speech hidden by an accidental cause outside the wording; its ruling is investigation to see if the hidden meaning expands or restricts the apparent.

In the Hanafi hierarchy of clarity, al-Khafi sits between al-Zahir (the apparent) and al-Mushkil (the problematic). This lesson unpacks its precise definition and ruling, drawing on the commentary of Noor al-Anwar. Understanding al-Khafi is essential for correctly applying general texts when particular instances are not explicitly covered by the wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition components
Break down the definition: speech (كلام), hiddenness of meaning (خفاء المراد), due to an accidental cause (عارض) that arises from other than the wording (غير الصيغة), and not attained except by investigation (بالطلب).
The key is that the cause is external to the wording.
2
Distinguish al-Khafi from al-Mushkil and al-Mujmal
If the hiddenness originates from the wording itself, it becomes al-Mushkil (problematic) or al-Mujmal (ambiguous). Al-Khafi's hiddenness is accidental, not structural.
This distinction is crucial for correct categorization.
3
Understand the ruling (hukm) of al-Khafi
The ruling is that it must be investigated (النظر فيه) to determine whether the hiddenness indicates an increase (مزية) or a decrease (نقصان) in meaning compared to the apparent.
If increase, rule according to the apparent; if decrease, do not rule (i.e., stick to the apparent meaning).
4
Apply to the theft verse example
The Quranic verse (5:38) uses 'thief' (السارق) which is apparent for a common thief. When applied to a pickpocket or grave-robber, hiddenness arises because such persons are not typically called thieves in usage. Investigation (ijtihad) includes them under the ruling, confirming an increase (extension of the rule).
If investigation suggested a decrease (e.g., excluding a specific instance), we would not rule on it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريف الخفي وحكمه
فقال: وأما الخفي: فما خفي مراده بعارض غير الصيغة لا ينال إلا بالطلب يعني أن الخفي اسم لكلام خفي مراده بسبب عارض نشأ من غير الصيغة؛ إذ لو كان منشؤه الصيغة لكان فيه خفاء زائد ويسمى بالمشكل والمجمل، فلا يكون مقابلاً للظاهر الذي فيه أدنى ظهور، ثم بعد ذلك نظر الشارح في هذا الجواب بأن فيه مسامحة؛ لأن قوله: "إلى شهر" لا يصلح أن يكون مفسرا لكونه غير مستقل بنفسه، ثم بعد ذلك أزاح ذلك النظر، وقال: مراد المصنف أن هذا الكلام يحتمل أمرين نكاحا ومتعة فرجحت المتعة فلا غبار فيه؛ لأنه ليس فيه نسبة كونه متعة إلى قوله إلى شهر" فتدبر . (السنبلي) فيكون متعة : أي فيكون نكاحاً مؤقتا فاسدًا كالمتعة؛ لأنه يكون متعة حقيقة، فإن المتعة تختص بلفظ التمتع كذا في كتب الفقه، ثم اعلم أن المتعة لا تجوز عند الأئمة الأربعة، وما في "الهداية" من نسبة حل المتعة إلى مالك فغلط كما ذكره الشارحون كذا في البحر الرائق . (القمر) إلا كونه متعة أي إلا كونه في حكم المتعة. (القمر)
وليس كلامًا مستقلا إلخ بل الكل كلام واحد ولا معنى للتعارض بين أجزاء الكلام. (القمر) في مقابلاتها في مقابلات أقسام الظهور، وهي أقسام الخفاء. (القمر) فما خفي إلخ : المراد بالخفاء في التعريف: الخفاء اللغوي، والمعرف الخفي الاصطلاحي فلا يلزم تعريف الشيء بنفسه. (القمر) نشأ من غير الصيغة يعني أنه ليس اختفاء في مدلول اللفظ بل عوض عارض في بعض الجزئيات اختفى بسببه أن هذه الجزئيات من أفراد مسمى اللفظ أم لا . (القمر)

بيان المتقابلات للأقسام الأربعة السابقة
٢٥٢
تعريف الخفي وحكمه فإن كلا من هؤلاء مترتب في الخفاء ترتب الأصل في الظهور، فإذا كان في الظاهر أدنى ظهور،
أي أقسام الخفاء في الشدة والضعف فلابد أن يكون في الخفى أدنى خفاء، وهكذا القياس فلا ينال مراده إلا بالطلب، فصار كمن
اختفى في المدينة بنوع حيلة عارضة من غير تغيير لباس وهيأة، ثم في قوله: "بعارض غير الصيغة" مسامحة، والأظهر أن يقول بعارض من غير الصيغة. كما في عبارة شمس الأئمة الحلواني، وقوله: "لا ينال إلا بالطلب" ليس قيدا ،احترازيا، بل بيان للواقع وتأكيد للخفاء. وحكمه النظر فيه ليعلم أن اختفاءه لمزية أو نقصان فيظهر المراد أي حكم الخفي النظر فيه وهو الطلب الأول ليعلم أن اختفاءه لأجل زيادة المعنى فيه على الظاهر أو نقصانه فيه، فحينئذ
المراد
أي بعد الطلب
يظهر المراد، فيحكم في الزيادة على حسب ما يعلم من الظاهر ، ولا يحكم في النقصان قط.
كآية السرقة في حق الطرار والنباش، فإن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا
(المائدة: ۳۸)
أدنى خفاء وهو الذي فيه أدنى ظهور، فمحل الخفاء في الخفي ليس هو نفس الصيغة، ومحل الظهور في الظاهر نفس الصيغة، فتغاير المحل فيهما، وهذا لا يقدح في تقابل الظاهر والخفي في مراتب الظهور والخفاء فإن الخفي فيما فيه خفي ليس بظاهر فيه، فلا يجتمعان في محل واحد من جهة واحدة. (القمر) وهكذا القياس ففي المشكل زيادة خفاء على الخفي كما في النص زيادة وضوح على الظاهر وفي المجمل زيادة خفاء على المشكل كما في المفسر زيادة وضوح على النص، وفي المتشابه خفاء كامل كما أن في المحكم وضوحًا كاملاً. (القمر) مسامحة: فإن قوله غير الصيغة بالجر لا يصلح أن يكون صفة لعارض؛ لأنه احترز به عن المشكل والمجمل
الخفاء بعارض؛ إذ لو كان منشأ الخفاء الصيغة لكان فيه خفاء زائد، فلا يكون مقابلاً للظاهر
والمتشابه، فيفهم منه أن الخفاء في هذه الثلاثة بعارض هو الصيغة وهو فاسد كذا قال ابن الملك لله. (القمر) والأظهر إلخ فإن العارض هو الناشي من غير الصيغة، وإنما قال والأظهر و لم يقل: والصواب لاستقامة كلام المصنف بأن يقال: إن قوله : غير الصيغة بدل من قوله عارض أي بسبب غير الصيغة كذا قيل. (القمر) ليس إلخ: فإن كل خفاء لا ينال المراد فيه إلا بالطلب. (القمر) للواقع فإن بعض قيود التعريف يكون واقعيًا. (المحشي) على الظاهر : متعلق بالزيادة أي على ما يفهم من الظاهر . (القمر)
أو نقصانه إلخ معطوف على الزيادة أي نقصان المعنى فيه عما يفهم من الظاهر. (القمر)
Definition of al-Khafi and its ruling. He said: As for al-Khafi, it is that whose meaning is hidden due to an accidental cause other than the wording, not attained except by investigation. Meaning that al-Khafi is a name for speech whose meaning is hidden due to a cause that arises from other than the wording; because if its origin was the wording, it would have increased hiddenness and would be called al-Mushkil and al-Mujmal, and thus would not be parallel to al-Zahir which has minimal appearance... Its ruling is to investigate it to know whether its hiddenness is for an (increased) merit or deficiency, so the intended meaning becomes manifest. So when it increases, it is ruled accordingly based on what is known from the apparent, and a decrease is never ruled. Like the verse of theft regarding the pickpocket and the grave-robber, for the statement of Allah Most High: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' (5:38).
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage defines the category of al-Khafi (the hidden) and explains its ruling. It begins by stating that al-Khafi is speech whose intended meaning is hidden due to an accidental cause (عارض) that arises from something other than the wording itself (غير الصيغة). If the cause of hiddenness had been the wording, it would be of a higher degree of hiddenness, called al-Mushkil (problematic) or al-Mujmal (ambiguous), and thus not be parallel to al-Zahir (the apparent), which has minimal appearance. The author then clarifies that the definition includes the qualification 'not attained except by investigation' which is not a limiting condition but a description of reality. The ruling (حكم) of al-Khafi is that it must be investigated (النظر فيه) to determine whether the hiddenness is due to an increased meaning (or an additional merit) or a deficiency (or reduced meaning) compared to what is understood from the apparent. After investigation, the intended meaning becomes clear. If the hiddenness is due to an increased meaning, the ruling is based on what is known from the apparent, but a decrease is never ruled upon. An example is given from the Quranic verse on theft (5:38): the word 'thief' (السارق) is apparent but when applied to a pickpocket or grave-robber, it is khafi because such individuals are not typically called thieves in common usage; investigation (ijtihad) is required to include them under the ruling. The commentary also contains a discussion about a previous example (nikah to a term) and corrects a misunderstanding about the permissibility of mut'ah marriage, stating that it is not allowed by the four Imams, and that a statement in al-Hidayah attributing its permissibility to Malik is a mistake.

Key Terms
الخفي (al-Khafi): Speech whose meaning is hidden due to an accidental cause other than the wording itself, requiring investigation.
العارض (al-'Aarid): An accidental cause that arises from outside the wording, causing hiddenness.
الطلب (at-Talab): Investigation or seeking to understand the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what distinguishes al-Khafi from al-Mushkil?
A) Al-Khafi is hidden due to the wording itself, while al-Mushkil is hidden due to an accidental cause.
B) Al-Khafi is hidden due to an accidental cause other than the wording, while al-Mushkil is hidden due to the wording.
C) Al-Khafi requires no investigation, while al-Mushkil does.
D) Al-Khafi is synonymous with al-Mujmal.

Key Takeaway
Al-Khafi is speech hidden by an accidental cause outside the wording; after investigation, rule on increase but not on decrease.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
intermediate
10 min
Definition and Ruling of al-Khafi (The Hidden Text)
Defining al-Khafi, its ruling requiring research, and its consequence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-Khafi, state its ruling requiring research (talab), and distinguish it from al-Zahir by identifying the external cause of hiddenness.

Core Idea
Al-Khafi: meaning hidden by external cause; ruling requires research to decide if meaning increases or decreases.

In the Hanafi hierarchy of textual clarity, after al-Zahir comes al-Khafi. Unlike a text that is merely apparent, the Khafi text has its meaning concealed by an accidental cause unrelated to its wording. The mujtahid must actively seek the intended meaning, and based on whether the hiddenness reveals an increase or deficiency in connotation, he derives the ruling accordingly. This lesson unpacks that definition and its legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
1. Position al-Khafi in the hierarchy
Recall that Hanafi usul divides clear texts into layers: al-Zahir (apparent), al-Khafi (hidden), al-Mushkil (difficult), and al-Mujmal (ambiguous). Al-Khafi sits between al-Zahir and al-Mushkil. Understand that just as al-Zahir has minimal clarity, al-Khafi has minimal hiddenness (adna khafa').
The author parallels the arrangement of clarity in al-Zahir to the arrangement of hiddenness in al-Khafi.
2
2. Identify the cause of hiddenness
The hiddenness in al-Khafi arises from an external accidental cause (arid min kharij), not from the wording itself. This cause is something like a conventional name change or a contextual factor that veils the literal application.
The author refines the definition: 'by an accidental cause other than the wording' – some commentators suggest 'from other than the wording' is more precise.
3
3. Grasp the ruling: research (talab)
The mujtahid must conduct research (al-nazar fih, al-talab al-awwal) to uncover the intended meaning. This research determines whether the hiddenness indicates an increase (ziyada) or deficiency (nuqsan) in meaning compared to the apparent (zahir).
The statement 'it is not attained except by seeking' is not a restrictive condition but a confirmation of hiddenness.
4
4. Apply the outcome of research
If research reveals an increase in meaning over the apparent, the ruling is extended accordingly (e.g., applying a more severe punishment). If it reveals a deficiency, the ruling is not applied (e.g., exempting from punishment). The principle: 'rule for increase, never rule for deficiency'.
This operational rule will be tested in the next lesson with the theft verse.

Source Text

بيان المتقابلات للأقسام الأربعة السابقة

تعريف الخفي وحكمه فإن كلا من هؤلاء مترتب في الخفاء ترتب الأصل في الظهور، فإذا كان في الظاهر أدنى ظهور، أي أقسام الخفاء في الشدة والضعف فلابد أن يكون في الخفى أدنى خفاء، وهكذا القياس فلا ينال مراده إلا بالطلب، فصار كمن اختفى في المدينة بنوع حيلة عارضة من غير تغيير لباس وهيأة، ثم في قوله: "بعارض غير الصيغة" مسامحة، والأظهر أن يقول بعارض من غير الصيغة. كما في عبارة شمس الأئمة الحلواني، وقوله: "لا ينال إلا بالطلب" ليس قيدا احترازيا، بل بيان للواقع وتأكيد للخفاء. وحكمه النظر فيه ليعلم أن اختفاءه لمزية أو نقصان فيظهر المراد أي حكم الخفي النظر فيه وهو الطلب الأول ليعلم أن اختفاءه لأجل زيادة المعنى فيه على الظاهر أو نقصانه فيه، فحينئذ المراد أي بعد الطلب يظهر المراد، فيحكم في الزيادة على حسب ما يعلم من الظاهر، ولا يحكم في النقصان قط.

كآية السرقة في حق الطرار والنباش، فإن قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا ﴾ (المائدة: 38) ظاهر في حق وجوب قطع اليد لكل سارق خفي في حق الطرار والنباش؛ لأنهما اختصا باسم آخر غير السارق في عرف أهل اللسان، فتأملنا فوجدنا أن اختصاص الطرار باسم آخر لأجل زيادة معنى السرقة إذ السرقة هو أخذ مال محترم محرز خفية، وهو يسرق ممن هو يقظان قاصد لحفظ المال بضرب غفلة وفترة تعتريه، واختصاص النباش باسم آخر لأجل نقصان معنى السرقة فيه؛ لأنه يسرق من الموتى الذي هو غير قاصد للحفظ، فعدينا حكم القطع إلى الطرار لأجل الزيادة فيه بدلالة النص ولم نعد إلى النباش لأجل النقصان فيه، ولو كان القبر في بيت مقفل قيل: لا يقطع النباش؛ لما ذكرنا، وقيل: يقطع؛ لوجود الحرز بالمكان وإن لم يوجد بالحافظ، وهذا كله عندنا، وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي : يقطع لكل سارق إلخ فحكم السارق خفي في حق الطرار والنباش لعارض من الخارج، وهو اختصاصهما باسم آخر يعرفان به (السنبلي لأنهما اختصا إلخ فتطرقت الشبهة في أنه يشملها اسم السارق أم لا، فتأملنا في المعنى الشرعي للسارق فوجدنا إلخ. (القمر) إذ السرقة إلخ : قلت : التعريف الجامع للسرقة: أخذ مال معتبر شرعًا، من حرز أجنبي لا شبهة فيه خفية، وهو قاصد للحفظ، في نومه أو غيبته احترز بالأول ما دون النصاب، وبالثاني عن الأخذ غير الحرز، وبالثالث عن ذي رحم محرم وبالرابع عن مال فيه شبهة الحرز كمال الشركة، وبالخامس عن والانتهاب، وبالسادس عن النبش وبالسابع عن الطرار. (السنبلي) :محترم أي معزز بأن يكون المال متقوما يحل الانتفاع به شرعًا، فلا قطع بسرقة خمر مسلم، وأن يكون عشرة دراهم، فلا قطع بسرقة أقل منها (القمر) محرز واحترز بقوله : محرز عن الأخذ من غير حرز، ويقول: خفية عن الانتهاب والغصب كذا قال ابن الملك. (القمر) بدلالة لأن الحكم إذا ثبت في الأدنى يثبت في الأعلى بالأولى. (المحشي) بدلالة النص متعلق بقوله فعدينا وفيه أن الحد للزجر، وزاجر الأدنى لا يثبت في الأعلى دلالة، ألا ترى أن الكفارة في قتل الخطاء لا تثبت في قتل العمد دلالة على أن الزاجر مشروع فيما كثر وقوعه، فلا يلزم شرعه فيما قل وقوعه كالطر، فإنه أقل وقوعا من السرقة، ولذا قال بعض شراح أصول البزدوي: إن إثبات القطع في الطرار بالعبارة؛ لأن المطلق يتناول الكامل فلأن يتناول الأكمل أولى. (القمر)
قيل: لا يقطع إلخ: هو الأصح كذا في "الدر المختار" وهو قول الإمام السرخسي كذا قال البرجندي. (القمر) لما ذكرنا أي لأجل النقصان في اللفظ، وكل من الناس يتأول في الدخول في ذلك البيت لزيارة القبر. (القمر) : وهذا أي عدم قطع النباش عند الإمام الأعظم وعند محمد رحمها. (القمر)
Explanation of the correspondences for the previous four divisions.

Definition of al-Khafi and its ruling: For each of these is arranged in hiddenness as the original is arranged in clarity. So since in al-Zahir there is minimal clarity (i.e., the degrees of hiddenness in intensity and weakness), it must be that in al-Khafi there is minimal hiddenness, and likewise by analogy. So one does not attain its meaning except by seeking. So it becomes like one who hid in the city by a kind of temporary trick without changing clothes and appearance. Then in his statement: 'by an accidental cause other than the wording' there is looseness. The more apparent is that he should say 'by an accidental cause from other than the wording' as in the phrase of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani. And his statement: 'it is not attained except by seeking' is not a restrictive condition, but rather a clarification of the reality and a confirmation of hiddenness. And its ruling is to reflect upon it to know that its hiddenness is due to an increase or a deficiency, so the meaning appears; i.e., the ruling of al-Khafi is reflection upon it—that is the first seeking—to know that its hiddenness is because of increase of meaning over the apparent (zahir) or deficiency in it. Then the meaning—i.e., after seeking—the meaning appears. So one rules regarding the increase according to what is known from the apparent, and one never rules regarding the deficiency.

Like the verse of theft regarding the pickpocket (tarrar) and the grave-robber (nabbash). For Allah's statement: 'The male thief and the female thief, cut off their hands' (5:38) is apparent (zahir) regarding the obligation of cutting the hand for every thief, but hidden (khafi) regarding the pickpocket and grave-robber; because they are distinguished by another name besides 'thief' in the custom of the people of the language. So we reflected and found that the distinction of the pickpocket by another name is for an increase in the meaning of theft; for theft is taking property that is respected (muhtaram), guarded (muhraz), secretly, and he steals from one who is awake, intending to guard the property, by striking with heedlessness and a passing state of weakness. And the distinction of the grave-robber by another name is for a deficiency in the meaning of theft; because he steals from the dead who do not intend to guard. So we extended the ruling of cutting to the pickpocket due to the increase in it by implication of the text (dalalat al-nass), and we did not extend it to the grave-robber due to the deficiency. And if the grave is in a locked house, it is said: the grave-robber is not cut off; for what we mentioned, and it is said: he is cut off due to the existence of guarding (hirz) by place even if not by guardian. And all this is according to us (Hanafis). And Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i said: He is cut off for every thief... etc. So the ruling of thief is hidden with respect to the pickpocket and grave-robber due to an external accidental cause, which is their being distinguished by another name by which they are known. (al-Sunbuli: because they are distinguished etc., so doubt arises whether the name 'thief' covers them or not, so we reflected on the legal meaning of thief and found... etc.) (al-Qamar) 'For theft is...' I say: The comprehensive definition of theft: taking property that is legally considered valuable, from a guarded place (hirz), by a stranger, without ambiguity, secretly, while the owner is intending to guard, whether in sleep or absence. By the first he excludes less than the nisab, by the second he excludes taking from non-hirz, by the third he excludes a mahram relative, by the fourth he excludes property with ambiguity of hirz like partnership property, by the fifth he excludes plundering and usurpation, by the sixth he excludes grave-robbery, and by the seventh he excludes pickpocketing. (al-Sunbuli) 'Respected' i.e., valued such that the property is of value (muttaqawwim) and permissible to benefit from legally; so no cutting for stealing a Muslim's wine, and it must be ten dirhams; so no cutting for less. (al-Qamar) 'Guarded' - he guarded by his statement 'guarded' against taking from non-hirz. And he said: 'secretly' against plunder and usurpation; so said Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'By implication' because when the ruling is established for the lower, it is established for the higher a fortiori. (al-Muhashi) 'By implication of the text' is attached to his statement 'we extended' and there is in it that the hadd is for deterrence, and the deterrence of the lower is not established for the higher by implication. Do you not see that expiation in accidental killing is not established for intentional killing by implication? That is because deterrence is legislated where occurrence is frequent, so its legislation is not necessary where occurrence is rare, like pickpocketing, for it is less frequent than theft. Hence some commentators on Usul al-Bazdawi said: The establishment of cutting for the pickpocket is by explicit wording (al-ibara); because the absolute (mutlaq) encompasses the perfect, so encompassing the more perfect is more appropriate. (al-Qamar)
'It is said: he is not cut off' etc.: That is the more correct (asahh) as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and it is the saying of Imam al-Sarakhsi; as said al-Barjandi. (al-Qamar) 'For what we mentioned' i.e., due to the deficiency in the wording, and every person has the interpretation of entering that house to visit the grave. (al-Qamar) 'And this' i.e., the non-cutting of the grave-robber according to Imam al-A'zam and according to Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the category of al-Khafi (the hidden) in the Hanafi hierarchy of textual clarity. It begins by defining al-Khafi: a text that is not immediately understandable but requires research (talab) to uncover its intended meaning. The author explains that al-Khafi is the opposite of al-Zahir (the apparent); just as al-Zahir has the minimum degree of clarity, al-Khafi has the minimum degree of hiddenness. The hiddenness arises from an external cause (arid) other than the wording itself. The ruling (hukm) for al-Khafi is that the mujtahid must investigate it to determine whether the hiddenness indicates an increase in meaning over the apparent or a deficiency. If it indicates an increase, the ruling is extended accordingly; if it indicates a deficiency, the ruling is not applied. This principle is then applied to the Quranic verse on theft (5:38). The verse is zahir for the ordinary thief, but khafi for the pickpocket (tarrar) and grave-robber (nabbash) because they have distinct names. Through research, the Hanafis conclude that the pickpocket steals from a vigilant person, thus his act has an additional element (increase), so he is subject to the hadd of cutting. The grave-robber steals from the dead, who have no intent to guard, thus his act is deficient in the meaning of theft, so he is not subject to cutting. This is the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i disagree and hold that both should be cut because the verse is general. The passage also discusses the condition of hirz (guardedness) and the dispute about cutting the grave-robber if the grave is in a locked house. The more correct view (asahh) according to later Hanafi authorities like al-Sarakhsi is non-cutting. This lesson demonstrates how the usul concept of al-Khafi is concretely applied in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
الخفي (al-Khafi): A text whose meaning is not immediately clear due to an external accidental cause, requiring research to uncover whether the hiddenness indicates increase or deficiency in meaning compared to the apparent.
الظاهر (al-Zahir): A text whose meaning is apparent without research, but still open to possibility of ta'wil (interpretation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of al-Khafi, what is the consequence if research reveals a deficiency in meaning compared to the apparent?
A) The ruling is applied cautiously with modifications.
B) The ruling is not applied at all.
C) The ruling is applied by analogy to similar cases.
D) The text is treated as ambiguous and left unresolved.

Key Takeaway
Al-Khafi requires research; if research shows increase, apply the ruling; if deficiency, do not.

Hanafi Text Clarity Hierarchy
